Record of the Academic Lecture by the Japanese Industrial and Political Delegation to China 107

Last afternoon, the Mayor hosted a banquet for all members of the delegation.

Diplomatic and industrial authorities from both China and Japan offered congratulatory messages.

According to the Central News Agency, the Japanese Industrial and Political Delegation to China, led by Dr. Kyoichiro Inoue, arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday. Yesterday at noon, Mayor Wu of this city held a banquet at the Chinese Arts and Crafts Society to welcome the delegation. After the banquet, a lecture meeting was held, presided over by He Baicheng. Diplomatic representatives from both China and Japan offered congratulatory messages. From the Japanese side, Hiroshi Maruyama gave a speech, and from the Chinese side, Zhao-huan Li delivered a lecture. The meeting adjourned around 4 p.m. Details are recorded below:

Mayor's Banquet: Yesterday at noon, Mayor Wu hosted a special banquet at the dining hall of the Chinese Arts and Crafts Society on Avenue Foch, to welcome the delegation. He also invited prominent figures from various circles in China and Japan to attend. Mayor Wu delivered the welcoming speech, translated by Guangfang Zeng. Then, Dr. Inoue, the leader of the delegation, gave a reply, translated by Xiu Wang. Guests and hosts mingled cordially during the banquet, which concluded at 2 p.m.

List of Delegation Members: The members of the Industrial and Political Delegation to China include: Masasuke Ide (Executive Director of the Automobile Manufacturing Company), Sukenozuke Hayashi (Major General, Director of the Osaka Army Arsenal), Tsuyoshi Kajii (Director of the Engineering Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, Lecturer at Tokyo University), Eisuke Yoshida (Trustee of the Ministry of Commerce and Industry), Naoki Takada (President of the Japan Industrial Association), Hiroshi Maruyama (Professor, Doctor of Literature at Nihon University), Morio Nakamatsu (Director of the Imperial Invention Association), Ryuji Yamada (Director of the Research Institute of the Minister's Secretariat of the Railway Ministry), Taketaro Matsuda (Rear Admiral of Naval Aviation, Head of the Japan Engineering Association), Ko Matsunaga (Permanent Member of the Industrial Conference, Executive Director of the Industrial and Political Association), Tsutomu Mihara (Vice Admiral of Naval Ordnance, Doctor of Engineering, Director of the Technical Research Institute of the Ministry of the Navy), Shigesada Sugi (Director and Chief Engineer of Sumitomo Metal Industries), Shuhei Iwamoto (Professor at Tokyo University, Member of the Aeronautical Research Institute), Shinji Kawahara (Agricultural and Forestry Technician of the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry), Juichiro Motono (Professor of Engineering at Kyushu University), Takenosuke Miyamoto (Doctor of Engineering, Technical Official of the Ministry of Interior), and others.

Guests at the Banquet: Those invited by Mayor Wu to attend included Ambassador Arima, Consul General Ishii, and other Japanese officials, leaders from business, cultural, and artistic circles in Shanghai; from the Chinese side, university presidents, deans, leaders of academic organizations, heads of cultural institutions, members of the Chinese Arts and Crafts Society, figures from banking and commercial sectors, totaling over seventy people, were personally hosted by Mayor Wu.

Mayor's Speech: At the banquet, Mayor Wu delivered a welcoming speech, stating: "Ambassador Arima, Dr. Inoue, distinguished guests, ladies and gentlemen, today we gather leaders from the academic and business communities of this city to welcome the Japanese Industrial and Political Delegation. As the host, I have prepared a modest feast to entertain you, and I am deeply delighted. The Japanese Industrial and Political Association is a highly reputable academic organization in Japan. The delegates are all renowned figures in academia. Dr. Inoue, the leader of the delegation, is a Doctor of Engineering and former Minister of Railways. His knowledge and experience have long been admired. It is a great honor to hear his insights today. This visit to Shanghai to hold academic lectures, with the depth of knowledge of these gentlemen, will undoubtedly provide valuable and specialized insights for the benefit of the academic community of this city. In modern times, academic pursuits in various countries have broken through the barriers of national boundaries and established close international connections. Although each nation has its unique characteristics, special national conditions, and different needs, based on the principle that 'stones from other mountains can polish jade,' no nation should 'shut itself off,' and no cultured nation should 'be self-righteous.' The progress of human culture in the past was largely due to mutual learning, mutual refinement, mutual borrowing, and mutual emulation. The future progress of world culture must depend on human mutual assistance and cooperation. Therefore, mutual assistance and cooperation are the ultimate goals of human evolution, while jealousy and strife are the sources of cultural destruction. China and Japan share the same script and are of the same race. In the past, the progress of culture, academics, economy, and society in both countries cannot deny the historical connection of mutual assistance and cooperation. Today, I have organized this grand gathering, hoping that the academic circles of China and Japan will not neglect this valuable historical connection, thoroughly recognize the ultimate goal of human evolution, and strive for the progress of Eastern national culture and academics in the spirit of cooperation. In particular, we should base our efforts on the virtue of mutual assistance to lay the foundation for peace in East Asia."

Inoue's Response: After Mayor Wu's welcoming speech, Dr. Inoue delivered a response, stating: "Today, nations are basing their foundations on industry. The two neighboring countries of East Asia should jointly develop industry. If both governments and peoples can adopt Western culture and integrate it with inherent Eastern culture, then in the future they will surely surpass the civilizations of Europe and America. Seeing the current international situation, it is not enough for just one country in East Asia to strive for progress. It is necessary for both countries to seek joint development in order to advance East Asian civilization. This visit to China is entirely based on this purpose. First, to exchange research and experience in academics between the two countries. Second, for both countries to work together to seek connections in industrial technology, increase the welfare of the East Asian people, and contribute to lasting peace. To achieve these goals, we are willing to fully share the difficulties and experiences that Japan has encountered in its past efforts with China for reference."

Opening of the Lecture Meeting: After the banquet hosted by Mayor Wu, the lecture meeting commenced, with Mayor Wu appointing He Baicheng as the chairman. The chairman delivered the opening remarks.

Chairman's Speech: Chairman He Baicheng delivered the opening remarks, saying: "Director Inoue, Mayor Wu, members of the Industrial and Political Delegation to China, distinguished guests from China and abroad, today the Japanese Industrial and Political Delegation to China and distinguished guests are holding an academic lecture meeting here. I am honored to be appointed chairman by Mayor Wu. Before announcing the purpose of the meeting, I would like to express a few thoughts in my capacity as chairman. First, we should thank Mayor Wu for not only treating us to a sumptuous feast but also giving us this good opportunity to exchange ideas. Second, we should welcome all the distinguished guests from China and abroad who are attending today, especially the members of the Industrial and Political Delegation to China who have come from afar. Third, we should especially welcome the two experts who are giving lectures today. I dare to predict that their lectures will be very valuable. The work of the interpreter is also something that cannot be done well without specialized scholars. We are very fortunate to have Mr. Zeng Guangfang here today to take on this role, and we should also welcome him. There is one more point that has caused me a personal and interesting difficulty. Today, I am not only the chairman of the lecture meeting but also the chairman of the Chinese Arts and Crafts Society. Since we are holding the meeting at the headquarters of the Chinese Arts and Crafts Society, I must also, as the chairman of the board of directors of the Chinese Arts and Crafts Society, take this opportunity to represent the board of directors of the Chinese Arts and Crafts Society and express our welcome to all the guests. At the same time, I must also, as the chairman of the meeting, represent today's guests and express our gratitude to the Chinese Arts and Crafts Society for lending us the venue. Now, let me continue to briefly explain the purpose of today's meeting. We all know that the various Eastern nations, although they have had a high level of civilization for thousands of years, have always had the problem of overemphasizing the spiritual aspects. For example, the three major thought trends of Confucianism, Buddhism, and Taoism in the East, although extremely noble and profound, inevitably focus on moral or spiritual cultivation and neglect material development. In order to adapt to the modern environment, we Easterners should devote some energy to the study of material things. Today's lecture meeting can be said to be a concrete demonstration of this trend. Secondly, the National Government and people of China are well aware of the importance of material construction and have been working hard to do so. For example, in recent years, the construction of aviation, railways, and highways has achieved remarkable results, which have been praised by Chinese and foreign people alike. However, in this era of rapid scientific progress, we must often exchange new experiences and valuable theories with experts from other countries to serve as reference for everyone. Today's lecture is an exchange of this kind of new experience and theory. Furthermore, we all know that the industry of our Eastern neighbor, Japan, is very developed, and it has made remarkable progress, especially in engineering construction. The members of the Industrial and Political Delegation to China who are attending today are all pioneers in this field. Their experiences of success and failure in this field are of particular value to China because of our shared language and culture. Therefore, today's lecture meeting can be said to be a gathering to promote material construction and exchange engineering knowledge. We can obtain a lot of valuable reference materials from this, so that the nations in our Eastern civilization system can keep pace and reach the stage of modernization. In addition, I believe that the international equality, understanding, and goodwill that Mayor Wu mentioned at the banquet can only be fully and effectively achieved through this noble work of knowledge exchange. This is the purpose of our meeting today. Now, because time is precious, we should begin to follow the scheduled agenda and invite the two experts to give their lectures. Before the lectures, we must first read the congratulatory telegrams from the authorities of the Chinese and Japanese governments to all the guests. We should first thank the Chinese and Japanese government authorities for their encouragement. Furthermore, today's newspapers reported that Mr. Li Zhao-huan was injured in an accident and therefore could not attend the meeting. We express our regret and condolences. Fortunately, he has already submitted his manuscript, which he entrusted to Mayor Wu to pass on to the delegation."

Foreign Minister Wang's Speech: After the Chairman's speech, Gao Zongwu, Director of the Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, representing Wang Zhaoming, who also served as Minister of Foreign Affairs, read the welcoming speech, saying: "Japan's rapid advancement in industry and the excellence of its manufacturing quality in recent years have been recognized worldwide. Therefore, our people deeply admire the Japanese people's technical genius and their diligent pursuit of science. The visiting gentlemen of the Industrial and Political Delegation to China are all leaders in the academic and industrial fields. I hope that after their observations, they will present their great theories and provide enlightenment. Our country is currently in a transitional era, and there is no other way to save the country than through science. I hope that our academic community will learn from the virtuous, think about aligning themselves, and be able to catch up, and sharpen their research, and use what they have learned to serve the country. Then the backwardness of the industrial world can be remedied with science, and the construction of the national economy can gradually achieve its success. The visit of the Industrial and Political Delegation to China will not only enhance the friendship between the people of the two countries, but it will also contribute to the development of the future of our country's industry. I respectfully offer this blessing and wish you all good health. October 26, 1935, Wang Zhaoming, Minister of Foreign Affairs."

Japanese Foreign Minister's Speech: Then, Ambassador Arima read the congratulatory message from Japanese Foreign Minister Koki Hirota: "On the occasion of the Japanese Industrial and Political Delegation's visit to the Republic of China, with the support of various circles in both China and Japan, and the opening of an open and joint lecture meeting under the joint authority of the academic communities of both countries today, it is truly a cause for celebration and congratulation. Looking back, I must say that there have been some regrettable missed opportunities for joint academic research, which is the most important thing for the development of humanities in the relationship between China and Japan. On the other hand, there is a lack of this kind of cooperation among the people, which has led to some estrangement in the relations between the two countries. This is something that the Minister deeply regrets. This state of affairs is like burying valuable books in the ground, or storing good rice and wealth in a warehouse. This is not because of loyalty to the truth and one's own country. Several years ago, at the International Industrial Conference in Tokyo, even though the relationship between China and Japan was still in a difficult period, many of your country's scholars humbly and frankly participated, which is enough to prove the enthusiasm of your country's scholars for the truth. We were already admiring them at that time. If we remove the emotions of the moment and follow the eternal historical laws, and remove the partial views and observe the overall situation from a high place, we can easily see that China and Japan should always have a relationship of mutual literature, mutual understanding, and mutual support. The ancients said that sincerity and rectifying the heart are the right ways to cultivate morality, and investigating things to attain knowledge is the way to pursue science. These two are originally two sides of the same coin and should not be biased. However, the problem of modern times lies in bias, and what East Asia is worried about is the lack of science. The independence of East Asia can only be achieved after the independence of East Asian industry is established, and the independence of East Asian industry can only be achieved after the scientific skills that East Asia lacks are fulfilled. The ancients said it well, 'Without education, there is no country.' For the past thousand years, our country has been striving to hone our original face by borrowing from your culture's annotations and reflections. Now, within the fields of pure science and applied engineering, we have reached the world's standards. If your country's government and people humbly and frankly recognize and accept this scientific ability of neighboring Japan, and both rely on each other, they can realize the development of a new civilization that is both refined and substantial, and that is both spiritual and material. This is something that the Minister firmly believes. However, this can be said to be the common obligation that we East Asia should bear within the broad community of the world. October 26, 1935, Foreign Minister Koki Hirota."

Japanese Minister of Commerce and Industry's Speech: Consul General Ishii also read the congratulatory message from Japanese Minister of Commerce and Industry Genji Matsuda, saying: "Today, at this time of an academic lecture meeting under the joint authority of the industrial circles of China and Japan, I feel very honored to have the opportunity to offer my respectful congratulations. The countries of East Asia have had close relations since ancient times, and their cultural exchanges have had a significant impact on each other. This is something that I don't need to elaborate on here. Especially in the recent situation, I feel the need for cooperation among the countries of East Asia. However, at this time, with the aim of contributing to the connection and cooperation of Eastern industrial technology and academics, it is timely and very beneficial to the Eastern industrial world to hold a joint lecture meeting between the two countries. This is certain and there is no doubt about it. The gentlemen participating in this meeting, please be aware of the purpose of this meeting, exchange your academics and knowledge with each other, and hope to achieve a very satisfactory result, so as to contribute to the upward development of Eastern industrial culture. This is what I most hope for. October 26, 1935, Japanese Minister of Commerce and Industry Genji Matsuda. There was also a congratulatory message from Chen Gongbo, Minister of the Ministry of Industry, representing Vice Minister Liu Weichi (omitted).

Academic Lectures: Then, the Chairman introduced Dr. Hiroshi Maruyama, a Doctor of Literature from Japan, and Li Zhao-huan, President of Jiaotong University, to give their lectures. Dr. Maruyama's lecture was titled "Industrial Education in Japan," and Mr. Li's lecture was titled "The Relationship between Engineering and Industry." Mr. Li was injured in a car accident the day before and was unable to attend, so he submitted his lecture manuscript to Mayor Wu to be forwarded to the delegation. (The speeches of both parties will be published separately.) At the end, Chairman He Baicheng delivered the closing remarks, saying: "Distinguished guests, now Mr. Hiroshi Maruyama's lecture has come to an end. Although we only had one gentleman's lecture, it was indeed able to fully express the purpose I described in my opening remarks. I believe that all the guests who attended today feel the same as I do, feeling very happy and very admirable. I now, in my capacity as chairman, express my gratitude to Mr. Hiroshi Maruyama on behalf of everyone, and congratulate them on the success of the lecture. At the same time, I would also like to take this opportunity to thank the several lecturers for their hard work, and the guests for their enthusiastic participation and unwavering attendance. Now we will adjourn the meeting, and I hope to see you all again tomorrow."

Continuing Today: After the meeting, Dr. Inoue, the leader of the Industrial and Political Delegation to China, asked Mayor Wu to convey to all the Chinese guests who attended yesterday that they are still invited to attend the banquet hosted by the delegation at the Chinese Arts and Crafts Society today for a friendly gathering, and to hold the second day of the lecture meeting. Ying, a professor at Tongji University in China, will lecture on "Industry in Shanghai," and Mr. Shuhei Iwamoto, a graduate in science from Japan, will lecture on "Japanese Aviation."

Continued News of the Two Ships in Distress: "Xin Feng" Towed Out... "Hai Hua" Salvaged 108

"Xin Feng" Towed to Safety

It was reported in yesterday's news that the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's "Xin Feng" encountered a hurricane, breaking its propeller shaft and losing a propeller blade, causing the ship to drift. On the evening of the 25th, the "Xin Feng" drifted to 35 degrees 05 minutes north latitude and 122 degrees 10 minutes east longitude, where it anchored, and the wind subsided slightly. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company immediately ordered the "Rui Shan" to sail from Lianyungang at 7 p.m. on the 25th. It arrived at the "Xin Feng's" location at 11 a.m. on the 26th and began towing it at noon yesterday. At 6:25 p.m., the "Xin Feng" was towed out and is now sailing towards Shanghai. Kangzhenji has sent a tugboat to wait outside the Wusongkou. Once the "Xin Feng" arrives, it will be towed into the Huangpu River, berthed at the South Bund Wharf to unload cargo, and then sent to the factory for repairs. However, the seas near Qingdao are still rough, and it is estimated that it will not arrive until this afternoon.

Surveying "Hai Hua"

Ji Chuanfang, the general manager of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's "Hai Hua," which sank after hitting a reef in Qingdao Port due to the wind, as reported in this newspaper, took the Jinpu train to Jinan yesterday morning to transfer to the Jiaoji train to Qingdao in order to personally survey the sinking of the "Hai Hua" and determine the strategy for salvage or abandonment.

Shanghai Chinese Cigarette Manufacturers Association Held Its 6th Annual General Meeting 109

Discussed Solutions to Mitigate the Impact of Smuggled Cigarettes on Business. The Shanghai Chinese Cigarette Manufacturers Association held its 6th Annual General Meeting at the Central Western Restaurant on 4th Avenue at 2 p.m. yesterday to discuss solutions to mitigate the impact of smuggled cigarettes on business. Details of the meeting are as follows:

Attending Members: Shen Weiting (Cuizhong), Gu Zhongying (Huapin), Wang Xingchong (Ruilun), Xie Ruiyang (Asia), Ju Gengsheng (Lixing), Wang Weilin (Ruilun), Qiu Tanglin (Great Southeast), Wu Linzhi (Hexing), Ge Xiongfu (Fuxin), Yao Weixiong (Hexing), Shen Dexing (Huacheng), Dai Gengxin (Huacheng), Wang Junzhi (Nanyang), Sun Lishan (Great East), Zhang Xinliang (Great Southeast), Tao Wenkui (Dexing), Shen Yankang, Wang Weiguan (Zhongnan), Shi Quan (Jiangzhe), Yao Shushen (Great East), Wu Peiyin (Youcheng), Li Xuedong (Huadong), Xia Richuan (Huapin), Wang Jisong (East China Sea), Chou Guanquan (Youli), Jing Yimeng (Huamei), Yu Luxin (Luxin), and Zhu Ya Kui, representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, Sun Mingqi, representative of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Jiang Yongyi, section chief of the Tax Office, and Chen Yan'yin, representative of the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Unified Tax Bureau, were present to provide guidance.

Chairman's Speech: After the meeting was opened as usual, Shen Weiting, Ge Xiongfu, and Shen Dexing were elected as the presidium. First, Chairman Shen Weiting reported, roughly stating that Chinese cigarette manufacturing has been declining to the extreme since its inception. The reasons can be divided into three points: (1) The overall economic downturn has affected business, resulting in sluggish sales; (2) Social economic bankruptcy and the livelihood of the common people are difficult, so hand-rolled cigarettes are rampant, which affects the cigarette business; (3) Since the British American Tobacco Company depreciated and dumped its products, Chinese cigarette factories have been unable to resist due to limited capital. All of these reasons are enough to promote the decline of Chinese cigarettes. In the future, we hope that everyone will work together to save the crisis of Chinese cigarettes, etc. Then, Shen Dexing reported on the income and expenditure for the past year, Ge Xiongfu reported on the association's affairs for the past year, and Sun Mingqi, the representative of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and Jiang Yongyi, the section chief of the Tax Office, gave encouraging speeches.

Discussion of Proposals: Then, the discussion began. (1) Due to the sluggish business relationship, the proposal to cancel the Lunar New Year gift of monthly spleen was passed in principle and handed over to the Executive Committee for detailed discussion and handling. (2) How to deal with the impact of smuggled cigarettes on business was resolved to be decided by the Executive Committee. The meeting was then adjourned.

General Overview of This Year's Flood Relief 110

Briefing by the Central Relief Committee and the Charity Relief Association

This year, the rivers were flooded, and the victims were all over the fields. The tragic situation is unbearable to describe. Compared with the flood of the past ten years, it is even worse. The affected provinces include Hubei, Hunan, Jiangxi, Anhui, Shandong, Henan, Hebei, and Jiangsu. Xu Shiying, the head of the delegation, personally went to inspect and received reports from the local authorities of the provinces. The affected counties and cities numbered 239, with an affected area of about 142,000 square kilometers. The number of affected people reached more than 20 million, and public and private losses are estimated to be more than 800 million yuan. In addition, there were also floods and droughts in Fujian, Guangdong, Shanxi, Shaanxi, Gansu, Ningxia, Guizhou, Sichuan, Chahar, Suiyuan, and Inner Mongolia. The water in Shandong has not yet receded, and Jiangsu, as the tail of the Yellow River, is expanding. This is the general situation of the affected provinces.

The Central Government is concerned about the flood victims and is in charge of relief. People from all walks of life in society are working together to provide assistance. First, the Central Government approved 1 million yuan of national currency from the Central Disaster Relief Reserve Fund and handed it over to the Relief Committee to work with the Ministries of Interior and Finance to allocate it to Hubei and other provinces to handle emergency relief and epidemic prevention. The Relief Committee also distributed in batches the relief funds donated from domestic and foreign sources and the relief donations remitted back by overseas Chinese, as they were received. As of October 21 of this year, a total of 340,278.69 yuan of national currency has been distributed to the provincial governments, provincial relief committees, the Relief General Association, and the Inner Mongolia Political Council in seven batches. The Shanghai Charity Relief Association for Flood Victims in Various Provinces allocated 540,000 yuan of national currency to nine provinces, including Hubei, for emergency relief. It hired heads of investigation and relief from various provinces to directly handle investigation and release matters, and repeatedly distributed 32,619 pieces of clothing and 348,468 pieces of emergency medicines to various provinces. This is the general situation of the relief work that the association has already carried out.

The Central Government is currently planning to issue 20 million yuan of disaster relief bonds. Other measures, such as the deduction of salaries of civil servants to assist in relief, may raise about 4 to 5 million yuan, which will all be used to handle work relief, cultivation relief, and agricultural relief in various provinces in the future.

Since its establishment, the Shanghai Charity Relief Association for Flood Victims in Various Provinces has been making every effort to raise funds. In the autumn of social and economic depression, it has received enthusiastic support from all walks of life, who have been frugal and brave in doing what is right. As of October 22 of this year, it has received a total of 273,659.76 yuan of national currency. However, the weather is now cold, and the severe winter is approaching. The victims in the disaster areas are without clothing or food, and relief is urgently needed. We are grateful that the organizers of the 6th National Games and the athletes from various provinces are concerned about the victims and held a swimming disaster relief performance on October 21 to raise money for relief. On the 26th, they held a football disaster relief performance, and we deeply appreciate their kindness and righteousness. We also thank the gentlemen and ladies from all walks of life for their enthusiastic participation and respectfully thank them on behalf of the more than 20 million victims.

It should be further emphasized that this year's flood is particularly severe, the disaster area is vast, and the victims are numerous, crying out for help and waiting to be rescued. In addition, the rebuilding of the Yangtze River embankment and the blocking of the Yellow River mouth are both urgent matters. We hope that our elders, brothers, sisters, uncles, and aunts will embrace the spirit of rescuing those who are drowning and fulfill their wish to save the people and the country by providing more assistance in terms of relief funds and supplies. This is what the victims pray for day and night.

Raven Submits Petition to the US Court in China for Bankruptcy 113

According to the Shanghai Evening Post & Mercury, Raven today (the 26th) submitted a petition to the US Court in China for bankruptcy. The petition lists liabilities of Shanghai currency $630,049.62, US$178,937.90, and British pounds £1,279. His assets, excluding private property claimed exempt, are worth Shanghai currency $264,000 and US$1,315. The petition states that he is willing to hand over all assets that should be allocated according to law to creditors for distribution and wishes to obtain the benefits of the Congressional bankruptcy laws. The secured claims (secured by securities) submitted by Mr. He Fu, the liquidator of three companies, including American Far Eastern Bank, are US$152,618.18, Shanghai currency $195,435.78, and British pounds £1,279. Unsecured claims total Shanghai currency $475,793.84, which is Raven's compensation from the three companies, including American Far Eastern Bank. Among the secured claims, US$26,319.72 is owed to Union Insurance Society of Canton, Limited, secured by Raven's property on Hongqiao Road, and Shanghai currency $10,000 is owed to Raven's lawyer, Evans, also secured by the property on Hongqiao Road. The property on Hongqiao Road is currently worth Shanghai currency $200,000, and other real estate is worth $64,000. Private property is worth Shanghai currency $2,967.71 and US$4,350. Life insurance, etc., is worth US$3,033 and Shanghai currency $2,967.71. Property claimed exempt from bankruptcy is worth a total of US$1,303. Raven's creditors are scheduled to hold their first meeting at the US Court next Tuesday at 10:00 AM.

Suspect in the Chien Teh Bank Case: Ou Jiancheng Flees; Court Strictly Pursues Guarantor to Fulfill Guarantee Obligation; Chen Xifu Avoids Confinement by Residing in His Hometown, Never Appearing in Court 114

Directors of the failed Chien Teh Bank, Chai Chuan-kuei and Supervisor Li Ching-wei, et al., were previously accused by the bank's creditors of fraud, etc. The First Special District Court has already rendered a preliminary judgment, imposing fines separately. For the four defendants who have consistently evaded, Ou Jiancheng, Chen Xiwu, Chen Fu-yi, and Zheng Huaigu, the trial has been temporarily suspended. It was later found that Ou Jiancheng did have a definite address in Shanghai and that he had already been sentenced to one year in prison by the First Special Court in a previous case involving the failed Wing On Bank, and was released on bail. Chen Xifu is hiding in his hometown of Yongkang County, Zhejiang Province. Neither is a person of uncertain whereabouts, so there is no need to suspend the trial. Therefore, the First Special Court issued summons. The defendants' defense lawyers were also instructed to inform their clients to surrender to the court pending trial. However, every time the court was scheduled to convene, Ou Jiancheng initially claimed to be ill. Upon hearing that the court had decided to send a forensic doctor to his home for examination, he fled in advance. Chen Xifu initially replied to his lawyer in a letter, stating that he would come to Shanghai to invest. However, he ultimately failed to keep his promise, and his whereabouts are now unknown. Yesterday afternoon, the court was scheduled to convene again. Judge Liu Yugui, because the defendants repeatedly failed to appear, asked Chen Xifu's lawyer in detail about Chen's Yongkang address to facilitate legal processing. Because Ou Jiancheng had already fled, the lawyer defending Ou did not appear in court yesterday. The court believes that Ou has already posted a satisfactory bond in another case, and now that Ou has indeed fled, the guarantor should be responsible. It is said that the court has been strictly pursuing the guarantor to fulfill the guarantee obligation in recent days. Therefore, the Chien Teh case will not be reopened until Ou and Chen, etc., are apprehended.

Using Forged Bills of Lading to Extract Rayon for Auction, a Total of Thirty Boxes Worth 15,000 Yuan; Zhang Jiaming Returned to Custody, Sentencing Scheduled 115

Zhang Jiaming, a Ningbo native collecting accounts for the Arnhold Trading Company on Szechuan Road, colluded with Wang Yi (who is at large) between June 3rd of this year to use forged bills of lading to send thirty boxes of rayon worth 15,000 yuan from the Arnhold Trading Company to the Lee Kee Auction House on Szechuan Road. Chen Bingzhang, a local who managed money, opened the boxes, changed the wrapping paper, and auctioned them off at a nominal price of 8,250 yuan. Afterwards, Zhang received a commission of 130 yuan, Wang gave a reward of 300 yuan, and Chen received a special commission of 30%, totaling 2,470 yuan. After the incident was discovered, Chinese Detective Jin Guanya of the Hongkew Police Station arrested Zhang and Chen successively and sent them to the First Special District Court. Their confessions have already been recorded in this newspaper. Zhang Jiaming was taken into custody, and Chen Bingzhang was released on a shop guarantee of 3,000 yuan. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiao Xie-fen opened the Criminal Court Three to continue the trial. Zhang Shizhu, a lawyer from the Public Works Department, stated that several witnesses from the Arnhold Trading Company and the Lee Kee Auction House had arrived in court and requested to be questioned. According to Chen Jigen, who works as a clerk at the Arnhold Trading Company, when the warehouse inventoried its stock at the end of June, it was discovered that thirty boxes were missing due to forged bills of lading. Mr. Flower of the west testified that rayon wooden boxes only have a triangular "wheat head" mark. The inner wrapping paper had twenty-five packages per box, and all had the "tiger" trademark. Next, Huang, the translator of Lee Kee Auction House, testified that he knew Zhang Jiaming. On that day, he and a customer named Zhao came and entrusted them to auction thirty boxes of rayon without the Arnhold Trading Company's mark. The commission was charged according to regulations at 75 yuan per thousand. Later, the money obtained from the auction was transferred by Chen Jiawu to Zhang Jiaming, etc. According to the staff member Lu Chang, the rayon was sent around 5:00 PM on June 3rd. The manager, Lee Kee Sheng, ordered the shop staff to open the boxes and change the wrapping paper for auction. According to the shop staff Zhao Qinan, the boxes had no Arnhold brand, only small marks. According to a Western employee named Zhu, the rayon wooden boxes and replacement wrapping paper were taken home by the manager after the fact and burned as firewood. The defendant Zhang Jiaming confessed that Chen Bingzhang knew the source of the goods completely. At that time, he gave the Westerners ten yuan and told him to find unmarked paper to rewrap the rayon. The work was completed around 8:00 PM. The money from the auction was delivered by him and Huang Ai-ting. Chen Bingzhang confessed that the rayon rewrapping was proposed by the manager, Lee Kee Sheng. According to Mr. Flower, the Western employee, the original wrapping paper had the Arnhold Chinese and Western characters in addition to the tiger trademark. Judge Xiao instructed the lawyer from the Public Works Department, Zhang, and the defendant's agent lawyers, Fan Gang and Fan Qisheng, to argue once and ordered Zhang Jiaming to be returned to custody. Chen Bingzhang was released on his original bail, and sentencing was scheduled for next Friday.

Woman Mao Zhiqing Sues Silk Merchant Zhang Zihe for Immorality and Abandonment; Zhang Zihe Did Not Appear in Court Yesterday 116

Mao Zhiqing, a woman from Zhenjiang, is currently twenty years old and resides at No. 41, Juqing Lane, Xinzha Road. She recently retained lawyer Yang Huchen to file a complaint with the First Special Court, accusing Zhang Zihe, who is engaged in the silk business, of immorality and abandonment. The gist of her lawsuit is that Zhang Zihe, with the introduction of Mr. and Mrs. Xi Rongsheng and Zhu Baozhu, proposed marriage to the plaintiff. On December 22nd of last year, he tricked her into signing a document and cohabiting. Initially, their relationship was harmonious and they loved each other very much. However, because Zhang did not complete the marriage formalities, the plaintiff attempted suicide on April 30th of this year and was revived after emergency treatment. On July 18th, the defendant also sent a letter to the plaintiff's parents, stating that he would hold a formal wedding ceremony in the shortest possible time. Because the plaintiff was deceived by sweet words, she patiently waited. Unexpectedly, the defendant left and never returned after the Mid-Autumn Festival. Not only did he abandon his former feelings, but he also did not care about her daily life, which is tantamount to abandonment. The plaintiff is in a foreign land, with no way to borrow money, and is weak and ill, so she is waiting for death. The plaintiff argues that the defendant's actions have violated Article 229, paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law, the crime of immorality, and Article 294 of the same law, the crime of abandonment. In addition to requesting the court to summon the defendant for interrogation, she also filed a civil suit, stating that because the defendant has assets of more than 100,000 yuan, he should be ordered to pay compensation of 20,000 yuan and living expenses of 100 yuan per month from September until the date of enforcement. The court approved the request. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Feng Shide came to Criminal Court One to summon the defendant. The defendant did not appear, nor did a lawyer appear on his behalf. Judge Feng briefly questioned the plaintiff, Mao Zhiqing, and ordered the case to be rescheduled for November 1st at 3:00 PM to summon the defendant to appear in court for questioning.

Man from Gongxing Lane Abandoned Child's Corpse, Sentenced to Punishment; Yang Sirens Sentenced to Three Months, Suspended for Two Years 118

Wang Zhushi, a Ningbo woman aged 38, residing at No. 120, Sheng Sheng Lane, South Qianjiatang, French Concession, is a lacquer worker. She has four children, boys and girls. Her youngest, the fourth daughter, was just born in July of this year. Due to congenital deficiencies, she was often ill and unable to afford medical treatment. She died at around 11:00 AM on the 23rd. Because Wang Zhushi could not afford a coffin and, as a woman, did not know the way or where to abandon the child's corpse, she found an old straw mat, wrapped the child's corpse, paid six jiao, and hired Yang Siren (48 years old, from Shandong), who lived in Gongxing Lane nearby, to take the child's corpse out for abandonment, promising to pay him a reward when her husband returned home in the evening. Yang then carried the straw mat containing the child's corpse out and abandoned it in an open space on Radou Road and Remy Road, not far away, at 4:00 PM that afternoon. He was discovered by a Vietnamese policeman who, suspecting a violation of regulations, took Yang to the police station. After hearing the story, the police chief sent Detective Yin Baoke to bring Wang Zhushi to the station. The child's corpse was sent to the morgue of the Tongren Hospital for examination. The next day, a report was submitted to the Second Special Court. Judge Wang Ren went to the scene and confirmed that the child had died of illness and ordered the Tongren Hospital to bury the body. The police station then sent Wang Zhushi and Yang Siren to Criminal Court One of the Second Special Court the day before yesterday. Attorney Gu Shouxi of the Police Department presented the case, filing a public prosecution for the crime of abandoning a corpse. After Judge Zhang Chaozuo questioned the defendants, he immediately announced the verdict in court, sentencing Yang Siren to three months of imprisonment, suspended for two years, and Wang Zhushi was found not guilty. After the judgment was rendered, both defendants were released in court.

Two Children Fighting; Zhu Dalong Dies 119

Zhu Dalong, the eight-year-old son of Zhu, a resident of Taiyuan Lane, Zhangjia Lane, Linping Road, Zhabei, was playing with Lu Xiaopangzi, a nine-year-old boy from a neighboring family, in the lane in front of his house the other day. For some reason, the two children suddenly started fighting, each refusing to give way. As a result, Dalong was defeated and knocked to the ground by Xiaopangzi, immediately losing consciousness and dying. The whole neighborhood was shocked. The post policeman took Lu Xiaopangzi, who caused the incident, to the station for temporary detention. Yesterday morning, the police officer Xu Jinlin was ordered to report to the local court for an autopsy. In the afternoon, Inspector Xiao Jin-ying, entrusted by the court, arrived at the scene with a coroner. The autopsy revealed that the deceased Zhu Dalong had suffered a fall on his left temple, which was determined to be the cause of death. The verdict was filled out and given to the family for burial pending instructions.

Suspecting a Friend of Abducting His Wife; Plotting Murder after Tricking and Binding Failed; Li Hongyu Recruits Thugs; Mi Qijiang Barely Escapes 120

Mi Qijiang, a 27-year-old day laborer from Taizhou, was unemployed and living in the home of his fellow villager and colleague, Li Hongyu, in Jia Du, Nanshi. Recently, Mi had found a job, so he found other accommodations and did not go to Li's home. Then, Li's wife suddenly disappeared after Mi left Li's house. Li suspected that Mi had abducted her and negotiated with Mi, but to no avail. Suddenly, late at night the other day, he tricked Mi into going to a shed at No. 53, Sanjia Lane, New West District, and, with the help of Mu Xiaobao, Mu Wu-xiao, Mao Guangcai, and others, tied Mi with a rope and poured a large amount of kerosene into Mi's mouth and nose, intending to murder him. Then, they carried Mi Qijiang to the Pudong riverside, threw him into the river, and attempted to destroy the corpse. Unexpectedly, they were discovered by a passerby. Soon after, a nearby police officer heard about it and arrived at the scene. After inquiring about the situation, he ordered the ropes to be untied. Mi Qijiang was able to move his hands and feet, but was already on the verge of death. Mu Xiaobao, Mu Wuxiao, and Mao Guangcai were arrested on the spot. However, when Li Hongyu was arrested, he used a small knife to cut open his head. The police saw this and quickly snatched the knife. He was then taken to the West Gate Precinct and detained after a preliminary hearing. Because the case involved attempted murder, he was ordered to prepare a document and be sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation together tomorrow afternoon.

Li Xiaobao and Li Fei's Case of Abuse of Private Punishment Awaits Further Investigation and Retrial 121

Zhao Yuanqing, from Jiangbei, recently filed a complaint with the Criminal Court of the local court, accusing Li Xiaobao, the leader of the North Station Detective Team, and Li Fei, a former detective, of abuse of private punishment and restriction of freedom. Judge Tan Zhuohong once summoned and interrogated them, and the details have been recorded in previous reports. It is learned that this case was continued by Judge Tan yesterday morning at 10:00 AM. On the defendant's side, lawyer Zhan Jifeng appeared in court to defend them. The plaintiff, Zhao Yuanqing, testified first, stating that he was passing by near Hongxing Road when he was taken to the team by Detective Li Fei, who extorted money from him. His father then entrusted his cousin Zhao Yuanshun to send the team leader ten yuan before he was released. Li Fei testified that he was ordered by the team leader to summon Zhao Yuanqing to the team and knew nothing else. Liu Jinrong testified that he saw Zhao Yuanshun hand over five paper dollars and five silver dollars. Finally, Li Xiaobao testified that he did not order Li Fei to summon Zhao Yuanqing. He also claimed that the cause of this case was that Li Fei, Liu Jinrong, and others were dismissed from their duties by order of the team leader, and they held a grudge against him. They secretly discussed at the Andong Hotel to frame him and requested an investigation so that the truth would be revealed. Furthermore, he produced a book of records of arrests, stating that the team must record all arrests. The judge obtained the confession and stated that the circumstances of the case were complex and that a further investigation and summons of witnesses was necessary for a retrial.

Results of Discussion by Telephone Experts: Scope of Investigation Lacks Importance; Extra Communication Fee in Chinese Area Should Be Cancelled to Lighten the Burden; Dual Calls and Call Forwarding for Long Distance Connections Must Be Reformed 122

According to the New Voice Press, the issue of telephone price increases in the Shanghai concessions has been under discussion by telephone experts from China, Britain, the United States, and Japan, hired by the Public Works Department, for two months. The report was telegraphed to the Public Works Department for review yesterday. The reporter from the New Voice Press specially sought opinions from relevant parties to serve as research for citizens. The details are described below:

Scope of Investigation Still Lacking in Importance

The Public Works Department first made an agreement with the telephone company that after the automatic installation was completed, it could revise the tariff schedule so that the company could have a net annual interest rate of 8.1%. This was already a fundamental mistake. The scope of investigation given to the experts this time, in short, was only to address whether prices should be increased and by how much. It rarely considered whether the use of telephones by the public was completely convenient and satisfactory under the telephone company's existing system. It is still difficult for the Chinese and foreign public to understand the position of the bureau. Furthermore, the expert report points out that the cost of the telephone company's conversion to automatic machines is enormous, and the ordinary and business expenses are alarming. This is indeed a fact, which shows that the company only knows that raising prices is the only way to increase revenue and does not know that cutting costs can also increase profits.

Toll Calls Should Be Eliminated

What telephone users in this city find most painful is the collection of extra toll calls between the concessions and the city. The report states, "We know of no precedent for users of telephone systems run by two authorities to be able to communicate freely without paying a fee." After investigation by all parties, this is not true. For example, in the case of the two telephone bureaus in Little Luzon, there is no charge for outside calls. Since the expert committee plans to adopt a pay-per-call method, it should advocate the immediate elimination of toll calls in order to save expenses and improve telephone services, which would be fair. Furthermore, direct dialing between the two districts is technically possible and there is absolutely no need to doubt it. However, the committee members have not been able to make practical suggestions on this point from an economic and technical perspective, which is a great regret for the citizens of this city. It is hoped that the telephone company and the telephone bureau authorities will improve the above two points in the shortest possible time.

Long Distance Connections Should Be Expedited

Long-distance calls made by users of the Shanghai Telephone Company must go through the long-distance stations of both the telephone bureau and the company. This doubles the procedure, which increases waste and costs time. This is rare in other countries around the world. If both authorities can adopt the experts' recommendations and abolish the long-distance station set up by the telephone company, so that the company's users can directly call the long-distance station of the Zhabei branch of the Shanghai Telephone Bureau, efficiency will definitely be improved significantly.

The Shanghai Chinese Race Club was established in 1926 and was suspended in the summer of last year. After more than a year, Mr. Du Yuesheng presided over the planning and restored all the original organization from before and invited those who loved horse racing to cooperate. The layout of the racetrack has many innovations and improvements. The members and the male and female guests in the public stands have very comfortable facilities. The stands have large and small restaurants, and the food and drinks are very rich and delicious. A rest room is specially set up for female guests. The horse ranch is located between the members and the ordinary stands. Before the race, all the famous horses can be seen at a glance. According to the person in charge of the club, those who go to the racetrack can take the Jiangwan Road through the Municipal Government District to Jun Gong Road and turn right, and they will arrive after a little more than a kilometer. The road along the way is flat, and the car ride is very comfortable. The club has a total of eight races today. There are five or six horses that are likely to win in each race, so there are many head-to-head bets and place bets. In addition, the club recently published a racing pictorial, which is dedicated to racing program lists, published every Saturday, and also includes various weekend entertainment and leisure activities, such as horse racing, dog racing, football, sports, movies, dancing, and all kinds of fresh news. Each issue sells for only 20 cents.

(3) This association is working to maintain the interests of the industry and strive for uniform market prices to secure the livelihood of businesses. We are currently designing and implementing this. Recently, due to the sharp and unabated increase in foreign prices, after investigating various stores engaged in cutthroat sales, it was found that there was no profit to be made. However, there is still internal competition among members, deliberately selling at low prices or disrupting the industry with overt price-cutting, potentially leading to disputes. If this continues, it will not be in the best interests of the industry. We are now reconvening to reassess and determine prices. Once printed, we will dispatch personnel to deliver them. We hope you will be informed and comply, and refrain from disrupting the market again. Otherwise, you may be subject to sanctions and penalties. This is an urgent notice.

We will then sort things out and submit them to the Municipal Council for record-keeping and future reference. From now on, the pullers registered under your name are yours, and the pullers registered under my name are mine. Limiting the random movement of pullers is a lifeline for us rickshaw companies. This association will also be helpless. I urge you a thousand times!

The Christian Methodist Episcopal Church: 50th Anniversary General Conference 132

The Conference Will Last Six Days, Starting on the 30th

Bishop Moore Has Arrived in Shanghai

The 50th Anniversary General Conference of the Chinese Christian Methodist Episcopal Church is scheduled to be held at the Moore Memorial Church on Xizang Road in this city on the 30th of this month. The Shanghai Diocese will also hold a meeting at the Moore Memorial Church on the evening of the 29th to welcome representatives from various regions. The following is an exploration of the preparations for the conference:

A Brief History of the Church

The founder of the Methodist Episcopal Church was the Englishman John Wesley. In 1784, the General Conference of the American Methodist Episcopal Church was formally organized in the United States and spread its teachings to various countries around the world. In 1848, two missionaries came to China and organized the Chinese Methodist Episcopal Church, raising funds to establish schools and hospitals. The country is divided into seven dioceses, with annual conferences held each year. The first conference was held in the 12th year of the reign of Emperor Guangxu of the Qing Dynasty. The meeting place was also in Shanghai. At that time, there were only two major dioceses: Shanghai and Suzhou. This year marks the 50th anniversary, and a grand conference is being held at the Moore Memorial Church in this city.

The Arrival of the Bishop

The conference is scheduled to last six days, from the 30th of this month to November 4th. Representatives from various regions have been arriving one after another. The conference will be presided over by Bishop Arthur J. Moore of the American General Conference. Bishop Moore arrived in Shanghai on the Empress of Japan ship on the 25th. Also arriving were Dr. W. F. Quillian, Director of the Department of Education of the General Conference, and Dr. W. G. Grma, Director of the Department of Evangelism. They are staying at No. 10 Jinglin Residence, Kunshan Road, Hongkou. It is also reported that Dr. Quillian took a train to Beijing yesterday afternoon, and Dr. Grma also traveled to Korea yesterday to inspect local church affairs on behalf of Bishop Moore. They will return to Shanghai before the 30th to attend the conference.

Today, at 2 p.m., we prepared an immediate check No. S 27410 of the Jing'an Temple Road branch of the Shanghai Bank, payable to the Tax Office of the Municipal Council, for 972 yuan and 36 cents, calculated based on a reasonable estimated value of 27,781 yuan, 8 jiao, and 3 fen. Zhenjiang Xu Clan Shanghai Association to Hold Dinner Today 136

The Xu clan of Zhenjiang has always been a prominent family. They have built a grand ancestral hall in their hometown of Yaoshi Temple. Every spring and autumn, they must remember their ancestors and hold grand ceremonies. However, many members reside in Shanghai due to their careers and cannot go to their hometown. Therefore, the Zhenjiang Xu Clan Shanghai Association was organized. Four times a year, they hold dinners in the West Hall of the Great China Hotel and perform sacrificial rites for the ancestors in the city where the guests are present. This summer, due to the hot weather, they did not have a suitable opportunity, which caused the dinner to be delayed. Now it is autumn, and Qi Yu, who is in charge of the Zi class, has left Shanghai and has not yet returned. But as winter is approaching, it is difficult to delay any further. It is said that they have consulted and agreed to hold the summer and autumn dinners today (the 27th) at 12 o'clock.

Traditional Chinese Medicine Practitioner Zhang Zhiren Sued by Concubine for Abandonment 137

Zhang Zhiren, a 45-year-old native of Songjiang and practitioner of traditional Chinese medicine residing at No. 86 Xiaoyou Lane, Bei Dang Road, French Concession, previously married a Cantonese woman, Ms. Li, as his concubine. Ms. Li is 24 years old. They lived together for nine years and had a son and a daughter, but the child passed away. Last year, Zhang took another concubine, and after she gave birth to a son, Zhang's feelings for Ms. Li gradually cooled, showing a tendency to favor the new and厭弃 the old. He disregarded her livelihood. Furthermore, after taking the new concubine, Zhang falsely claimed to Ms. Li that he needed money to buy land in the countryside and asked her to temporarily hand over her jewelry for his use, promising to return it later. Ms. Li believed him and handed over the jewelry to Zhang. However, Zhang immediately gave it to his new concubine to wear. When Ms. Li found out, she argued with Zhang, and he assaulted her. On the 29th of last month, at around 6 a.m., the two quarreled again over a trivial matter. Zhang used an iron ruler to beat Ms. Li, causing injuries, and then confined her in the room, not allowing her to go out. On the 6th of this month, Ms. Li took advantage of Zhang's absence to see patients and escaped in the evening to her relatives' house. The next day, she asked a fortune teller to write a petition on her behalf and submitted it to the prosecutor's office of the Second Special District Court, requesting a medical examination. She also filed a private prosecution against Zhang Zhiren in the criminal court for assault, with an attached civil suit seeking monthly living expenses of 50 yuan and medical expenses. She requested that the court investigate the matter according to the law. Upon receiving the petition, the court, yesterday morning, had Judge Qiu Huanjing preside over the trial in the Second Criminal Court and summoned both parties to appear in court. First, the plaintiff, Ms. Zhang Li, described the circumstances of the assault and abuse. The defendant denied the assault, stating that the plaintiff often went out and did not return when he was ill. He advised her, but not only did she not listen, but she also took the opportunity to run away without a trace. He had already reported this to the police. He now requested the court to allow the plaintiff to be taken back by a civilian. The judge told the defendant that the court's forensic doctor had confirmed that the plaintiff had injuries. If she did not want to go back, he could not force her. It would be better to settle the dispute amicably. He also stated that if a settlement could not be reached, the hearing would be rescheduled for 9 a.m. on November 4th, and then adjourned the court.

Policeman Openly Smoking Recorded with Demerit, Violating New Life Movement 138

Police Officer Wan Di, stationed at the front gate of the Guan Sheng Yuan Farm in Caohejing, was openly smoking a cigarette while on duty. He was spotted by an inspector who immediately reprimanded him, stating that he had violated the New Life Movement and tarnished the reputation of the police. The inspector immediately reported this to Director Cai, who was very angry. In addition to recording a major demerit for the officer, he also issued a notice to all the chiefs of the subordinate stations, instructing them to inform their personnel.

Wang Xin Attacked with an Axe 139

A Tragedy Before the Wedding

Nephew Commits Violence; Who Is Behind It?

Wang Xin, a resident of the Fahua Town in Western Shanghai, has a wife and children. Recently, he became involved with a young woman from Qibao, surnamed Mou, and rented a place for her at No. 27 Haige Lane, Haige Road. In order to please her, Wang arranged a banquet at the Great Shanghai Restaurant in the town yesterday (the 26th) to announce that he would officially cohabit with her. Unexpectedly, a tragedy occurred. The night before last, at around 6 p.m., Wang was lured to the door of his house by someone claiming to have something to discuss. Without asking any questions, the person took out an ax and hacked at Wang twice, once on the left shoulder and once on the back, causing deep wounds. Seeing that his purpose had been achieved, the assailant abandoned the ax and fled. Fortunately, Wang was able to return home with assistance. After examining the wounds, it was determined that they were not life-threatening, and he went to the hospital for treatment. According to some, the assailant was Wang's nephew (the nephew of his brother). Wang often provided financial assistance to the nephew. It is suspected that he was instigated by someone to commit this act. However, Wang's family members are keeping silent about the matter, so the cause is unknown.

Apprentice Injured by Car 140

Guo Minping, a 16-year-old native of Ningbo, is currently an apprentice at the Shen Yuji Machine Shop at No. 100 Danyang Road. Yesterday morning at around 8 a.m., Guo was on his way to work at the Yufeng Yarn Factory. When he was passing Yangshupu Road and Dengyue Road, a No. 9 bus suddenly came speeding towards him. Guo was unable to dodge in time and was knocked to the ground, injuring his head and arms. He was bleeding profusely and appeared to be in serious condition. He was then rushed to the Sacred Heart Hospital by the police in a vehicle for treatment.

Southern Automobile Company Causes Accident: Dodge Sanlun Car, Hits Car and Injures Person 141

Yesterday evening at around 7 p.m., a Southern Automobile Company business car, license plate number 12706 in the concession and 4034 in the Chinese territory, driven by driver Yuan Xisheng, was traveling east when it encountered a Sanlun car coming from the opposite direction. The distance between them was only two steps. Yuan, fearing an accident, quickly turned the steering wheel to avoid it. He was then taken to the Sacred Heart Hospital by the street police in a vehicle for treatment.

Wife Found After Escaping, Beaten and Injured: Ai Chen and Others Accused of Abduction, Extortion, and Assault 142

Zhang Jiudi, a 31-year-old farmer residing at No. 5, Lane 1378, Longhua Road, Western Shanghai, has a wife, Ms. Yang, who is 18 years old. On June 20th of this year, Ms. Yang used the excuse of returning to Ningbo and left without returning. Zhang believed her at first and did not pay attention until her parents came to ask for her, and he realized that she had run away. He then asked people to search for her everywhere, but to no avail. The day before yesterday, Zhang's cousin, Tang Lisheng, ran into Ms. Yang on the road with a woman coming out of a movie theater. Upon greeting her, he learned that Ms. Yang was being hidden by Ai Chen, a local woman residing at No. 15 Ai's House on Zhongshan Road. Ai had also introduced her to Xia Caigou, a Chongming native who sells soybeans (Xia is 36 years old and lives in Ai's woodshed). Tang immediately informed Zhang Jiudi, and they went together to pick her up. However, Ai Chen came out and stopped them, demanding 50 yuan for food expenses. Zhang replied that he had no money on him and would send it later, but Ai refused. Ai then gathered many gangsters, dragged Zhang into a small teahouse to negotiate. When they disagreed, they started assaulting him, causing serious injuries to Zhang's chest. Tang Lisheng reported this to Police Sergeant He Hanchen of the Triangle Land Police Station. Upon receiving the report, He immediately led police officers to the scene. The perpetrators had already scattered and fled. Ai Chen, Xia Caigou, Zhang Yang, and Tang Lisheng were taken back to the Xujiahui Police Station. After a brief interrogation by Director Chen, the case was deemed to involve accusations of abduction, extortion, and assault, and the file was immediately prepared and sent to the Bureau for investigation.

Other criminal cases: 22 cases, 39 suspects. Total: 275 cases, 452 suspects. All the arrested criminals have been preliminarily interrogated by the Third Section. With the exception of 96 people who were either dealt with according to the administrative penalty law for minor cases or sentenced and released, the remaining criminals have been transferred to the local court or other competent authorities for trial. The number of criminal cases arrested this week decreased by 43 cases compared to last week, and the number of arrested criminals decreased by 65.

Yesterday's Disaster Relief Soccer Game: Hong Kong Loses to Portugal 2-4; Hong Kong Suffers in the First Half, Conceding Four Goals; Makes Effort to Counterattack in the Second Half, Regaining Two Goals 154

In order to appeal for the disaster victims in various regions, the Flood Relief Association invited the Hong Kong team, the champion of this year's National Games soccer tournament, and the well-known Portuguese soccer team in this city to hold a charity match at the City Center Stadium at 3:00 PM yesterday. Two to three thousand people attended. The Hong Kong team carried the remaining power of the National Games, while the Portuguese had many veterans of sand court matches. The strengths of both sides were originally quite substantial, but it was a pity that Hong Kong was missing Li Huitang, a forward, no different from a headless snake; and the defense was missing Bao Jiaping, which was the same as giving others an opportunity. The Portuguese team attacked from the north to the south, and the nomads rode their horses from the north. They had already gained the advantage of the weather. The Hong Kong team was tired from continuous battles and like a heap of loose sand without harmony among the people. Thus, the Hong Kong team ended the first half with a score of zero to four. Fortunately, in the second half, everyone embraced a do-or-die spirit and constantly planned to wipe out their shame. They broke the cauldrons and sank the boats, working together harmoniously. The battle situation immediately became magnificent, and the overall situation gradually became clearer. They were able to regain one goal. However, the opportunity did not come again, and they eventually suffered a setback with a score of two to four.

The Portuguese Army's Ferocious Onslaught

After the start of the battle, the Portuguese, with the help of the fierce northeast wind, had a very strong morale. One could see the white-clothed men with the cross emblem jumping and chasing deer in the Central Plains. The blue-clothed, white-lettered athletes of Xiangdao (Hong Kong) suddenly had a situation of being unable to attend to both ends. They only held a chaotic battle situation and had no ability to resist. Thus, the enemy's left inside forward, L. Rocha Liao, scored a goal, opening the record. After the Portuguese gained the first goal, their spirit was further boosted. The ball often hovered in the Hong Kong team's position. Soon, the Portuguese center defender, Kao Qitan, took a long shot, which was intercepted by the left winger, Ada Ye, who penetrated along the side and kicked it hard. The Hong Kong goalkeeper, Huang Huaji, did not dare to neglect and quickly pounced to save, but he slipped and lost control, allowing the Portuguese center forward, Ke Lasha, to take advantage of the opportunity and push the ball into the net. Continuing the battle, the Portuguese army became even more arrogant. The right inside forward, Luo Tuo, picked up the ball and sent it to the front of the Hong Kong team's goal. The right inside forward, Liang Xianzhan, originally intended to head the ball out of bounds, but unexpectedly committed suicide, causing the ball to rush into the net, resulting in a score of three to zero. After this, although the Hong Kong team launched a counterattack once, it failed and was instead captured by the Portuguese team, with Ke Lasha scoring another goal, ending the first half with a score of four to zero.

Counterattack Yielded Little Effect

After Hong Kong and Portugal switched sides and fought again, the Hong Kong army was filled with righteous indignation, and the forwards were very active. Moreover, with the help of the wind, they were like tigers with wings. Zheng Jiliang entered and exited the million-strong army as if he were in no man's land. In a few minutes, the Portuguese team's virginity was broken by a Hong Kong team forward with a "zigzag" pass, headed by Zheng Jiliang, clear and crisp like never before, making it four to one. After this, although there were many good opportunities, there were also frequent misses. Ten minutes later, Cao Guicheng attacked the enemy's right wing position, and the center forwards also lined up in a goose formation to echo remotely. Cao dribbled to a suitable point and then hit the road to the center, and the Portuguese city was broken again. After that, the Hong Kong team was aggressive, and Tan Jiangbai was transferred to center forward, making the momentum even stronger. The Portuguese army's morale was slightly reduced. Unfortunately, the time had expired, and the counterattack ultimately failed, finishing the game with a score of two to four. The lineup is as follows:

Today's Jiangnan University Tennis: Guanghua and Fudan Finals 157

Yesterday, Central Abandons, Guanghua Defeats Chi Zhi 3-2

Fudan Wins Over Jinan, Championship Hopes are Quite High

The 9th Jiangnan Eight University Tennis Championships opened yesterday afternoon at Guanghua University on Daxi Road. This year's participants include five schools: Central, Guanghua, Chi Zhi, Jinan, and Fudan. Last year's champion, Jinling, did not participate due to circumstances. In yesterday's matches, Guanghua originally met Central, and Chi Zhi had a bye. Unexpectedly, Central was absent at the last minute, so Guanghua directly competed with Chi Zhi yesterday. As a result, Guanghua relied on the victory of the final doubles match to eliminate Chi Zhi 3-2 and win the final rights. Fudan then won a singles match and overwhelmed Jinan, also winning the final rights. According to the rules, the doubles match no longer needs to be played, but both sides continued to hold it to show sportsmanship. Fudan won both doubles matches again, resulting in a score of 5-0. Guanghua and Chi Zhi have equal skills and strength. Both sides are good at blocking the net and have excellent performances. However, Chi Zhi committed too many suicides, which was the main reason for the failure. As for the battle between Fudan and Jinan, both singles and doubles formed a one-sided situation. Fudan has many talents this year, such as Sun Qifang, Huang Jinju, Xu Zengrui, Peng Shaoxue, Feng Yipei, Guo Shaokai, and Huang Andao, who are all veterans of the sand court in the Xianfang Cup. No wonder Jinan returned in defeat. The second match between Guanghua and Chi Zhi, which was originally scheduled for 9:00 AM today, has been canceled because Central abandoned yesterday and Guanghua has already won the final rights. The final between Fudan and Guanghua will start at 2:00 PM this afternoon and will still be held at the Guanghua Stadium. Fudan has the highest hopes for winning this championship. China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture Grants 300,000 Yuan for Compulsory Education 159

Decision Made to Distribute in Two Equal Annual Installments

Next Annual Meeting to be Decided by Executive Committee

Second Annual General Meeting Held Yesterday

The Board of Directors of the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture held its second annual general meeting yesterday morning at 9:00 AM at the Cangzhou Hotel. In addition to work reports, it was decided to subsidize 300,000 yuan in educational expenses. Details are noted below:

The Board of Directors of the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture held its ninth regular board meeting at 9:00 AM yesterday (the 26th) at the Cangzhou Hotel on Jing'an Temple Road to discuss subsidizing compulsory education expenses totaling 300,000 national currency. The meeting adjourned at 4:00 PM. Details are noted below:

Directors in Attendance　The ninth regular board meeting was held yesterday morning at 9:00 AM. Attendees included directors Cai Yuanpei, Zhou Yichun, Becker, Hu Shi, Leighton Stuart, Li Yuying, Xu Xinliu, Sun Ke, Ding Wenjiang, and Ren Hongjun. Observers included US Ambassador to China Johnson, Ministry of Education representative Guo Youshou, Ministry of Foreign Affairs representative Yu Ming, and the foundation's acting secretary-general Sun Hongfen, totaling more than ten people.

Reports on Foundation Affairs　Chairman Cai Yuanpei presided over the meeting. Honorary Secretary Hu Shi first reported on the secretary's duties, followed by a report on foundation affairs on behalf of the executive committee. Honorary Treasurer Zhou Yichun reported on accounting matters, followed by Ren Hongjun reporting on foundation affairs for May and June, and Sun Hongfen reporting on foundation affairs after June.

Resolutions on Various Proposals　Matters for discussion: (A) Proposal to amend the foundation's rules of procedure. Resolved: Approved as amended. (B) Proposal to amend the foundation's articles of association. Resolved: Approved as amended. (C) Proposal to subsidize the Ministry of Education's promotion of compulsory education. Resolved: A subsidy of 300,000 yuan in national currency for compulsory education expenses, to be paid in two equal annual installments. Due to this proposal, this year's expenses, including 82,000 yuan in revenue and expenditure, will be handled by the executive committee to find ways to prepare. (D) Proposal to investigate primary and secondary education in China. Resolved: To proceed with the matter. Motions from the floor: (1) The date and location of the next meeting will be decided by the executive committee. (2) In accordance with the amended rules, Xu Xinliu and Becker were appointed as vice chairmen of the board. (3) In accordance with the amended rules, Xu Xinliu, Becker, and Sun Hongfen were elected as members of the Finance Committee. The meeting was then adjourned.

Cai Yuanpei's Banquet　After returning to Shanghai from Qingdao on the 3rd, Member of the Central Committee Cai Yuanpei presided over the ninth board meeting of the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture at the Cangzhou Hotel on Jing'an Temple Road yesterday. Last night at 7:00 PM, he hosted a small banquet at Yuyuan Road for attendees such as Ren Hongjun. It is rumored that Mr. Cai will stay in Shanghai for a day or two before going to Beijing to attend the Sixth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee.

Departing Separately　Hu Shi, Ding Wenjiang, Zhou Yichun, and others who traveled south specifically to attend the ninth regular board meeting of the foundation, will take the overnight express train to Beijing and then to Ping tonight at 11:00 PM, as the meeting is over. Ren Hongjun, the newly appointed president of Sichuan University, will remain in Shanghai to negotiate the construction of Sichuan University. He plans to take the train to Beijing tomorrow to discuss matters with the Ministry of Education before departing for Sichuan.
