Clear Weather: Jiangsu Boy Scouts Formally Inspected Yesterday 160

Chen Guofu Served as Chief Inspecting Officer

Tang Changyan Memorial Cup Presented

(Zhenjiang Correspondence) The sixth Jiangsu Provincial Boy Scout Inspection and Camporee entered its second day yesterday. The cold wind subsided slightly and the weather improved. All scheduled items proceeded smoothly. The formal inspection was held at 9:00 AM, with Chen Guofu serving as the chief inspecting officer. After the inspection ceremony, a silver cup was presented to Tang Changyan, the founder of the Jiangsu Boy Scouts. Chairman Chen presided over the presentation ceremony. Course competitions were held in the afternoon, and all events were very exciting. The elementary school group held a campfire meeting at 7:00 PM, and the secondary school group held a speech contest. Course competitions will be held this morning and afternoon, and a lantern parade will be held in the evening. The camp will be closed on the 28th.

Inspection Held

The inspection ceremony was held at 9:00 AM. Attendees included Chairman Chen Guofu, Director Yu Jingtang, Director Zhou Fohai, Commissioner Wang Boling, Ye Xiufeng, Executive Committee Member Zhou Shaocheng, Jiangsu Boy Scout founder Tang Changyan, General Association representatives Zhao Fansheng and Yang Pinji, Provincial Government Secretary-General Luo Shishi, Security Department Director Xiang Zhizhuang, Provincial Government Section Chief Wan Junmo, Education Department Section Chief Wu Jianzhen, Chief Referee Li Qifan, representatives from various agencies and organizations, referees, staff, and journalists, totaling over a hundred people. After the bugle sounded and the flag was raised, Chief Commander Song Jingchu reported to the inspection platform. A total of 171 Boy Scout troops, numbering 5,480 people, were present. After the Chief Commander's report, Boy Scouts carrying flags led the inspection personnel down the inspection platform for a week-long inspection. Each troop stood at attention and saluted as they passed by. The military bearing was solemn and the order was well-maintained. After the inspection, a parade began. As the entire group passed the command platform, they marched in step, looking to the right and saluting. After marching for a week, they stood at attention in front of the inspection platform.

Speeches by Officials

After everyone stood at attention, Chief Inspecting Officer and Central Representative Chen Guofu delivered a speech, stating in brief: "Seeing your spirit today reminds me of the current critical situation of the nation. The rise and fall of the nation depend most importantly on the youth. Boy Scouts can abide by the oath and regulations and serve the society and the nation in the future. To save the nation from peril, it depends on whether the youth can win honor for the nation and the people. Boy Scouts must not only abide by the regulations and oaths, but also study hard to acquire sufficient knowledge to serve society in the future, and they must also have a spirit of sacrifice. Only then can the nation have hope of prosperity." General Association representative Zhao Fansheng spoke about technical errors made by some Boy Scouts during the inspection and parade. The Provincial Party Committee member and chairman of the conference spoke about (1) Boy Scouts must be able to endure hardship, (2) Boy Scouts must aim to serve society, (3) They must bear great responsibility for the Chinese Nationalist Party, (4) They must consistently maintain the spirit shown during the provincial inspection. Provincial Government representative Wang Boling spoke about the relationship between Boy Scouts and the Chinese Nationalist Party. Tang Changyan, the founder of the Jiangsu Boy Scouts, expressed his hope that the Party and the government would continue to support the Boy Scouts.

Flag Raising

Jiangsu Boy Scout Inspection Command Platform

Presentation of Memorial Cup

After the speeches, Chairman Chen personally presented the Jiangsu Provincial Boy Scout Council with a large silver cup to be given to Tang Changyan, the founder of the Jiangsu Provincial Boy Scouts. Mr. Tang has founded the Boy Scouts for nearly 20 years, working tirelessly day and night. All Jiangsu Boy Scout staff members took this action to honor his virtue and repay his contributions. The large silver cup presented yesterday was about two feet tall and engraved with the words "Mentor of Youth." Mr. Tang personally accepted the cup. In addition to the silver cup presented by the Provincial Affairs Council, Troops 1123, 107, and 277 each presented a silver shield. In addition, various troops presented bamboo items, mirror frames, and other items, in large numbers.

Meeting of the Medical Education Committee of the Ministry of Education 161

The Medical Education Committee of the Ministry of Education held its first plenary meeting at the Ministry of Education at 9:00 AM on the 25th (the committee had held several simple meetings before the establishment of the three committees for nursing, midwifery, and primary and secondary school health design). Attendees included Liu Ruiheng, Weng Zhilong, Zhao Shiqing, Yan Fuqing, Huang Jianzhong, Gu Shusen, Jin Baoshan, Zhu Zhanggeng, Hu Ding'an, Song Wusheng, Zhu Hengbi, Yang Chongrui, Qu Jinqin (represented by Wang Zhaoju), and observers such as Lu Dexin, totaling more than ten people. Yan Fuqing chaired the meeting, Guo Changsheng recorded the minutes, and the following matters were discussed: (1) The Minister submitted for discussion a proposal from the Shanghai Pharmaceutical Industry Association requesting the establishment of a pharmacology talent village in the field of medicine and health. Resolved: After investigating, this case belongs to health and school administration issues. Health and medical education institutions have already established as much pharmaceutical talent as possible, so there is no need to discuss it further. However, the issue of pharmacology education is very important. Consultant Zhu Hengbi, Commissioner Zhao Shiqing, and Consultant Song Wusheng are appointed, and Secretary Zhu is invited to join the discussion of pharmacology issues, and to pay attention to what system should be in place to cultivate pharmacology talent. A draft should first be prepared and sent to the standing committee for discussion. (2) Please decide on the list of names for the medical education survey. Resolved: This survey of the teaching situation of each medical school will be handled by the secretary and commissioners of this committee, and professors and experts will be asked to join the group as soon as possible. The method of dividing into groups will be determined by the commissioners of this committee who attend the annual meeting of the Chinese Medical Association. Commissioner Huang Wen, Consultant Zhu Hengbi, Secretary Zhu Zhanggeng, Consultant Yang Chongrui, Specialist Wang Yihui, Commissioner Yan Fuqing, Commissioner Niu Huisheng, and Mr. Qi Shounan are designated to be responsible for this survey. The principle of the six-group method for general teaching survey is approved, and the list of candidates will be decided by the standing committee. (3) Please decide on the list of members of the textbook outline review committee. Resolved: After each school submits the trial textbook outline and notes their opinions, the standing committee will determine the review subjects and the list of review committee members. It can also be discussed at the principals' meeting to be held next year. (4) How should the editing and reviewing of medical textbooks be carried out? Resolved: Consultant Zhu Hengbi, Commissioner Zhao Shiqing, and Secretary Zhu Zhanggeng are designated to formulate detailed methods, and Mr. Lu Dexin is invited to participate and submit it to the standing committee for review. (5) Commissioner Yan suggested that the Ministry of Education issue a notice to all medical schools to submit the various books used for teaching for review. Resolved: Approved.

Recent News on the Translation Work of the National Compilation and Translation Bureau 162

The following is a summary of the translation work of the National Compilation and Translation Bureau in the past month: (1) The book "The Legacy of Greece" is a collection of papers by British experts exploring Greek culture, totaling twelve articles. Several translations have been completed, and the bureau plans to translate all of them. (2) The first draft of the seven-volume "History of English Literature" has been completed and is now being revised. It will soon be completed. (3) All fourteen volumes of mathematical terms have been approved by the Mathematical Terms Review Committee of the Chinese Mathematical Society and will soon be submitted to the Ministry of Education for publication. (4) The first ten parts of chemical terms in chemical engineering terms, totaling approximately 8,000 terms, have been organized and will be sent to various experts for review. The names of chemical instruments and equipment have already been preliminarily reviewed by various experts and will be organized within the year. (5) In the biological terms, the embryology terms have been submitted to the Ministry of Education for publication. Recently, Wang Zengjia has sent 1,597 term cards for botanical terms from Ping. (6) In the medical terms, the first proofreading of the bacteriology and immunology terms has been completed, and the second proofreading is in progress. The complete manuscript of the anatomical terms, totaling 522 pages, has been printed and will be sent for review. The psychiatric pathology terms will soon be fully organized and revised to prepare for submission for publication. The preliminary classification work of the pathological terms is in progress. (7) The meteorological terms are being edited by Hu Huanyong of Central University, and recently Wang Weiping has been invited to assist in the editing to ensure that the manuscript is completed as soon as possible. (8) The psychological terms are being edited by Wu Nanxuan and Zhao Yan, and recently Zuo Renxia, professor of psychology at Henan University, has been invited to assist in the editing. It is expected that the first draft of the general psychology terms will be completed by the end of November.

Notice Regarding Copper Molds for General Use: Must Be Handled According to Regulations 164

Reproduction or Sale of Movable Type in the Same Style is Prohibited

The Bureau of Education is Ordered to Notify All Bookstores

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education issued a notice yesterday stating: "According to Order No. 14536, Department of Public Education, Ministry of Education, Year 24, all sectors needing Zhuyin copper molds must follow the regulations in the 'Notice Regarding the Purchase of Zhuyin Chinese Character Copper Molds' and prepare the price to purchase from the Ministry or order from the Shanghai Zhonghua Book Company. The Bureau has been ordered to forward the notice to inform all parties. According to Article 6 of the Notice, before five sets of copper molds have been sold, all reproduction or sale of movable type in the same style, as well as those who have not submitted the molds to the Ministry for approval and have directly produced them, are prohibited. The meaning is very clear, but it is feared that various printing companies, stores, etc. have not fully understood and violated the current regulations, leading to investigations and prohibitions. You are instructed to forward this notice to all printing companies and bookstores in the city for compliance. This is of utmost importance. This order, etc. You are hereby notified to inform all printing companies and bookstores in the city for compliance, as necessary."

The Little Man (75) 165

— Original by Ms. Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

"Are you willing to compete with me?" Nanen said, eager to show off her skills.

Tao Mo leaned against the wall, looking very tired, and said, "It's too hot."

Nanen's sharp eyes glanced from one face to another. Seeing that Taifei was frowning, she asked, "What's wrong, Taifei?"

Jieke replied with a contemptuous expression, "The ball hurt his hand; he cries out at everything."

"I don't, I never do, no matter how much pain I suffer; crying out is just like a little Shi Bao," Nanen said, with a kind of haughty air.

"Taifei was provoked by that criticism and replied: Pshaw, I can make you cry in two minutes."

"See if you can!"

Taifei pointed to a tree with hard thorns by the wall and said, "Then go pick a thorn from that."

Nanen immediately "pinched the handful of thorns," pulled it out, and still held it in her hand with an "I'm not afraid of anything" air, even though the severe pain was almost unbearable.

"You're really amazing," the children shouted in unison. They naturally changed their attitude when they saw that a girl could have such courage.

Page 14

Spring and Autumn Children's Weekly

How to Use Opportunities to Read Living Books 166

— Ling

Reading is divided into rote learning and active learning. What is rote learning? What is active learning? Let me explain slowly.

We usually study at school, listening to teachers in class and discussing with classmates after class. All of this is knowledge gained from books. We should sincerely accept the knowledge in books because there are many things in books that we cannot see or hear in our daily lives. Reading books will help us know them. However, to gain broad knowledge, we must search in this great environment. Knowledge gained from books will only help us know but not thoroughly understand, so doubts often remain in our minds. Studying books exclusively without experimenting is rote learning. So how do we learn actively? We should research and investigate all phenomena in our daily lives according to what is said in books, and see if the experiments are the same as what is said in the books. Knowledge gained from such experiments can be deeply imprinted in our minds and will never be forgotten.

All inventors have invented various things through research and experimentation. They not only win glory for their country, but people all over the world benefit from them.

Children! Do you want to be inventors? Then you should work hard at studying and strive to research during this precious childhood. If you can invent things in the future, you will not only benefit society but also win glory for the Republic of China. At that time, you will think of the benefits of active learning.

Model Child 167

— Zhou Xian

Xiao Sizi is a poor child. His father is a worker who sells his labor, and his mother is a poor woman who helps others with work. Living in such a poor family, he naturally has no right to study. But Xiao Sizi loves to study very much. Although he has no money to go to school, he always feels envious when he sees children carrying schoolbags to school on the street.

But this autumn, the small school across the street from his home suddenly opened a literacy school. Unexpectedly, Xiao Sizi was forced to go to the literacy school to study, despite his father's strong disapproval. Studying was exactly what Xiao Sizi wanted, so he went to school in a hurry on the first day of school.

Although Xiao Sizi is only eight years old, because he is eager to learn, he studies literacy very seriously, so his grades are the best in the class of fifty people. Many old men and women in their fifties and sixties scored behind him. This made Xiao Sizi so happy that he woke up laughing from his dreams.

Because Xiao Sizi now knows hundreds of characters and has learned some rules at school, he is not as wild as he was when he was not studying. He knows how to bow when he sees people and speaks politely. Although the clothes on his body are still so old and worn, he washes them himself every two or three days, so he is not as annoying as before. So, a neighbor, Mr. prepared to introduce him to a shop to learn a trade.

Yesterday, I met him and asked him what he had been doing these days. He said: "These days, I am preparing a story about the Xinhai Revolution. I am preparing to go on stage to give a speech. Although my speech is less than ten minutes long, the teacher said that I spoke very well when I practiced yesterday. Sir, would you be interested in hearing my speech that day?"

Xiao Sizi was originally a wild child, but after studying for two months, he completely changed. He knows etiquette, can give speeches, can read vernacular essays, and will become an apprentice in a shop. Although his background is very poor, I think this is a very good model for children.

The Knowledge of Tears 169

— Bingyu

How do tears come about? This is a little knowledge that we should understand. When we are sad, tears flow out unconsciously, and tears also flow out when we are extremely happy. In other words, tears flow out when we are mentally stimulated or when the mucous membrane of the eyes and nose is stimulated. But what kind of thing are tears? Now I will tell you the physiological reason. Each of our two eyes has two lacrimal glands, and these lacrimal glands are the place where tears are produced. The amount of production varies with the seasons. The amount of production is not much in spring and autumn, and the amount of production is the most in extremely cold and hot weather. Tears are secreted from these four lacrimal glands. Tears have a great effect on the eyeballs. They can prevent the two eyeballs from drying out, keep the eyeballs fairly moist, and smooth the movement of the eyeballs. If the production of tears stops temporarily, the eyeballs will lose their freedom of movement, and the eyes will not be able to turn up, down, left, or right. Moreover, the eyeballs will also rupture. When dust and small organisms fly into the eyes, the eyes feel very uncomfortable, and the eyelids will move and tears will flow out, completely washing the eyeballs and letting the dust flow out of the corners of the eyes with the tears, and the eyeballs will not be damaged. Therefore, tears have a great effect. The lacrimal glands are near the inner canthus, passing through the lacrimal duct and flowing into the nasal cavity to become nasal mucus. If we feel very unhappy, we often cry and tears flow together, because being unhappy stimulates the "sympathetic nerve," the blood vessels immediately expand, and the surrounding muscles suddenly contract, compressing the lacrimal glands, and tears flow out continuously. As for the composition of tears, they contain one percent salt, as well as protein, carbonic acid soda, etc., so when tears flow into the mouth, they feel salty. You should never drop tears into food when you are eating, because it is extremely unsanitary.

Capturing Monkeys 170

— Kangjianzhaifu

Humans are considered the most intelligent beings in the world, but while monkeys are not as clever, they love to imitate. Humans take advantage of this imitative nature to catch them.

Legend has it that in the past, many wild monkeys inhabited Hengshan and Jianshan in Nantong. Living in the mountains and forests, they were originally harmless and caused no offense to humans. At the foot of the mountain, there was a teacher who gathered students and taught. The monkeys, seeing this from afar in the forest, waited until school was dismissed in the evening, then sneaked into the school. The larger monkeys dressed up as the teacher, and the smaller ones pretended to be students, messing with the books, brushes, and ink. By the time people arrived the next day, they had already vanished. At first, the teacher didn't understand and thought it was just naughty students causing trouble. Several of the more vocal students were repeatedly wrongly punished.

But despite the punishments, the mischief continued. The teacher grew increasingly suspicious and decided to investigate secretly. He discovered that it was indeed a group of monkeys doing this. After seeing this, the teacher came up with a plan. He cut out many small red paper circles and ordered the students to stick them on their eyes, pretending to play hide-and-seek. He also instructed the students to wear wooden clogs meant for rainy days to school, but to leave the clogs in the school when they went home.

The teacher left many red paper plasters on the desk and prepared a few villagers to lie in ambush with weapons. Sure enough, after class was dismissed, the monkeys sneaked into the school one by one, imitating the students by wearing the wooden clogs and sticking the red paper circles on their eyes. They were having a great time when suddenly, shouts arose from all sides, and the villagers came forward with weapons. The monkeys, with their eyes covered by the plasters and wearing wooden clogs, ran around blindly, and were captured one by one. This was considered revenge for the wrongly punished students.

Abacus and Knot-Tying 171

— You Mojun

"In ancient times, government was conducted by tying knots." Big events were recorded with large knots, and small events with small knots, to aid memory where it fell short. Different colored ropes were used to record different kinds of events. This has already been roughly described in the article "The Story of Knot-Tying" (published in this journal on September 29th). However, human wisdom is constantly developing, never stopping. Things once considered very convenient are often later found to be less applicable. Knot-tying is one such example.

As knot-tying became less practical, clever people came up with ways to improve upon it. According to Western scholars, the abacus we use today evolved from knot-tying. The abacus has rows of bamboo rods with beads strung on them. Originally, these rods were ropes, and the beads were the knots. This method of aiding memory is naturally much more convenient and applicable than knot-tying, and people gladly adopted it.

So, what did the earliest abacuses for recording information look like? This is difficult to determine. They were probably very crude, perhaps simply twigs bent into beads with a few ropes tied on them, nothing as refined as the abacuses we have today. The ones we use now have nine, eleven, or thirteen rows. Each row has seven beads. The top two beads are separated by a horizontal bar. Below the horizontal bar, each of the five beads counts as one. This later development came about because as human affairs became more complex, people's wisdom increased, leading them to invent this ingenious tool for counting. From then on, it was used for counting and no longer for recording information. This is a segment of the evolution from knot-tying to using the abacus, and it is a natural evolution.

Waste Utilization 173

— Qin Weinong

—Broken Light Bulbs Can Be Made into Fish Tanks—

This idea was mentioned in an article in this newspaper before, but the method of making it was not clearly explained. After reading the article, I was struck by a mischievous idea. One evening, with nothing to do, I found a few broken light bulbs and started experimenting. I broke two in a row and was quite surprised! I kept trying with renewed vigor, and calmly used my brain, and finally succeeded in my experiment. I dare not keep this secret to myself, so I wrote this article to share with my dear little friends. When you have nothing to do, you might as well try it!

(1) Materials—A broken light bulb (the filament should be broken, but the bulb should not be cracked).

(2) Tools—A knife, an awl, a small pair of scissors, and a basin of clear water.

(3) Instructions—First, use the knife to carefully cut off the lacquered cap at the top of the bulb. Then, fill the copper ring with water, hold the bulb firmly with one hand, place it in the basin of water, and use the awl to firmly strike the center of the bulb's core, causing the filament to break off. (Be careful not to let the bulb touch the bottom of the basin when striking). Then, use the scissors to cut away the glass connecting to the filament inside the water, cutting close to the copper ring to create a round hole. At this point, remove the filament from the bulb. Use thread to secure it tightly to the copper nails on both sides of the copper ring. Put some water in the bulb and raise one or two small goldfish. Isn't it a very fun fish tank?

Note—When striking the filament with the awl, the copper ring must be filled with water, because the light bulb is not truly empty. The water on top will reduce the external air pressure, and the bulb will not break.

Why Be Punctual? 176

— Jun Peng

"Being unpunctual" is an old habit of us Chinese people, so naturally, Chinese children are no exception. Dear little friends, do you want to be "unpunctual" children? If not, start being punctual from today onward—the reason why Chinese people are unpunctual is that they did not develop the habit of "being punctual" in their childhoods. Therefore, children! You must pay absolute attention to this issue of "being punctual"!

Why be punctual? It's because time does not return. Mr. Zhu Ziqing said it very well: "When the leaves wither, they have a time to turn green again; when the swallows leave, they have a time to return; when time goes, does it have a time to come back? Smart one, tell me, is there a time to come back?" Although I am not smart, I dare to say that time does not return.

What are the benefits of being punctual?

First, it doesn't waste time. For example, if we are taking a bus that leaves at 2:00, if you arrive at the station at 2:15, the bus will have left, and you will have to wait for the next one. Wouldn't you have wasted a lot of time in between? If you are punctual, this won't happen, isn't that the advantage of "being punctual"?

Second, it doesn't delay things. If you are not punctual and miss the bus, you won't be able to reach your destination, and the work you need to do will be delayed. If it's something important, something that affects the bigger picture, wouldn't it delay many people's affairs? If you are punctual, this won't happen, isn't that the advantage of "being punctual"?

Third, it maintains order. For example, if a meeting is scheduled for 9:00 AM at a certain place, but some members arrive at 8:30 AM, and others arrive at 9:30 AM, wouldn't that make the meeting place chaotic? How can there be order? If you are punctual, this won't happen, isn't that the advantage of "being punctual"?

Fourth, it increases efficiency. Because if you are not punctual, the work you do will definitely not be more than other people's. If a punctual person does two things, you can only do one thing. If you are punctual, this won't happen, isn't that the advantage of "being punctual"?

In summary, we know that if we are punctual, we can save time, not delay things, maintain order, and increase efficiency. Children! I hope you will always be punctual!

The Story of the White Mountain Crow (7) 177

— Xi

I quickly asked, "Madam, may I ask where these things are?" The magpie replied, "In my Green Palace, my love, you can see how we live there. There are over a hundred of us in total, and we are not like the large magpies in the villages, who often beg on the roads. We are all of noble lineage, slender and lively, none as big as a fist. Our bodies always have no more and no less than seven black stripes and five white stripes, this is an unchangeable rule, and we look down on all other races. You indeed do not have black stripes, but your quality is Russian, which is enough to let you enter the door of the Green Palace. We live our lives by doing two things: chatting and grooming. We groom from morning to noon, and chat from noon to dusk. We each perch on a tree, the taller the better, and the more ancient the more wonderful. In the middle of the forest stands an extremely large and fine elm tree, unfortunately, no one lives there. It is the former residence of the tenth generation of Queen Magpie (i.e., magpie). We often go there on pilgrimages, sighing and lamenting; but although we carry a light melancholy of nostalgia, our time is spent extraordinarily happily. All the wives there are very virtuous, and the husbands are not jealous. Our happiness is pure and real, because our hearts are very open, just like our speech, which is very straightforward. Our personalities are all very proud. If a hooded crow or other lowly species intrudes among us, we will all rise up together and peck at him mercilessly, but we also treat good neighbors very favorably. Therefore, we often prepare to help the sparrows and goldfinches who live in our small forest, sharing food with them and helping them resist external enemies. There is no place in the world where you can find a race as talkative as us, and none that speaks as well. In short, we live in happiness, nobility, conversation, and grooming."

I replied, "Madam, this is indeed the best there could be. I would not disobey any command you issue, but before I follow you, please allow me to say a word to this good girl." Then, I turned to the dove and said, "I beg you to tell me truthfully, do you really think I am a Russian magpie?"

Closing selling prices were $33.50 for spot, $0.25 for October, $2.25 for November, $1.50 for December, and $30.875 for January, with the buying price increased by 0.000625.

The Market's Plight Reaches Such Extremes 180

The prior day saw many long-term contracts, with some being rolled over at the original amounts and others requiring interest payments that were difficult to meet. One major factory had a long-term loan of $300,000, and when closing its books at the end of April in the first half of the year, it had already included $1,500 in interest as principal. The remaining three or four hundred odd dollars were paid on account. For the current period's interest, there was an additional $16,000. The creditor demanded payment of over $30,000, covering the principal and interest from the previous two periods. The debtor wanted to include the interest and principal and requested an additional $17,000 or $18,000 to round the total to $350,000. It was reported that the creditor conceded to payment of the current period's interest, but the debtor still claimed it was currently impossible to raise such a large sum to pay the interest. If the creditor refused to compromise, the debtor would have to accept the consequences. Such situations were reportedly numerous. It was also said that short term loans, both those that were maturing yesterday and those due at the end of the month for which interest payments were being demanded early, amounted to no less than $3 or $4 million. Aside from the principal, which was generally rolled over without issue, the interest alone totaled $140,000 or $150,000. With only three or four days remaining until the end of the month, it is unknown how many more disputes will arise.

Increased Special Margin Requirements for Margin Yarn and Cotton 184

Yarn up $8... Cotton up $3; Recently, the yarn and cotton markets have been driven by the gold market frenzy, rising sharply day after day, like runaway horses. In order to maintain stability, the Yarn and Cotton Exchange authorities will, starting Monday, October 28, increase the special margin requirement for new yarn purchases by $8 per bale and for new cotton purchases by $3 per dan. Both sides of the transaction will be charged on their inventory.

Grains; Gold Prices Soar Unabated; Flour and Wheat Rise Sharply by About Ten Cents; Grain Exchange Implements Special Margin Requirements; $800 for Soybeans and Wheat; $400 for Oilcake 189

The flour market has suddenly experienced an unusual surge, creating a serious situation, and the high prices are unprecedented. The only reason for the sharp rise is the unabated increase in gold prices, which has forced all commodity prices to rise. In recent days, because actual sales have been flat, investors have not been aggressive. Therefore, the rise in gold prices has only been in the range of three to five cents. However, yesterday, because speculators considered flour prices to be very favorable, they aggressively bought up the market. From the opening to the close in the morning, prices soared by five or six cents, and over 800,000 bags were traded. In the afternoon, the opening price increased because speculators were still buying as much as possible. The market continued to rise by another three or four cents, and 700,000 or 800,000 bags were traded. The increase in the January contract reached $0.1025, and the remaining months also increased by eight or nine cents. The danger of the situation is not difficult to imagine.

Page 16

Women's Corner

Marriage and Childcare 193

— Wuwei

All social phenomena evoke endless emotions. This place seems like a wondrous garden, either overgrown with weeds or with fruit trees planted upside down. Looking at just two things, marriage and childcare, there's this kind of meaning. Children are society's new life, new hope. At a time when families that are barely able to feed themselves are increasingly disintegrating, childcare centers are so necessary for the working masses who go out to find food all day long. However, the city of Shanghai, which proudly possesses hundreds of thousands of female workers, only has one "First Labor Childcare Center" on Penglai Road, and its actual situation, according to yesterday's newspaper, is like this:

"Since its opening a year ago, the center has provided care and education for the children entrusted to it, and has been highly praised by parents. Unfortunately, its location is far from the factory area, and due to limited funding and other reasons, the children entrusted to it cannot be purely from the working class. Currently, the center has 30 children entrusted during the day, with a fee of two dollars; and 10 children entrusted day and night, with the fee increased from eight dollars to twelve dollars."

In Shanghai, there are more than 100,000 children who are not cared for and need to be entrusted. However, the center can only accommodate this number, and it can be asserted that none of them are from the working class. So, the children of the working class either tire out their mothers, who cannot spare the time and die together with them, or crawl, wander, and die like insects. The mortality rate of children in our country is already at the same high level as India, a nation on the verge of extinction. We can imagine how dangerous it is! However, society's indifference to it can be said to be unsurpassed.

But on the other hand, society is vigorously emphasizing marriage. Each province and city is afraid that unmarried men and women will be restless, so they are vigorously helping them to find happiness and promoting convenient and economical group marriage systems. Since Shanghai initiated this last year, Tianjin, Nanjing, Guangzhou, Hangzhou, Zhenjiang, and Kaifeng have successively implemented it, and there is a trend of spreading throughout the country. At each wedding, the elegant and beautiful figures of the newlyweds and the grand ceremony attended by the officials truly arouse people's interest and make them eager to try. Although sports are said to save the country, the average daily audience of ten thousand can never compare with the grand occasion of each group marriage. If anyone says this is a "marriage movement," it is unlikely to be opposed. The prevailing trend has aroused even seventy-year-old men. As for society's intense focus on the marriage of a certain celebrity, the engagement of a certain swimming star, or the love affair of a certain soccer star, this is even more the end of the trend.

Marriage is an important part of life, and society's emphasis on it has its own reasonable reasons. But thousands of years of traditional thinking have led women to regard marriage as the only major event in their lives—there is nothing else. And recently, due to the evil waves of economic recession, the purchasing power of men in the marriage market is very weak, and there are countless unmarried young ladies. They have already suffered enough from melancholy in their daily lives, so how can they withstand the strong stimulation of group marriages? Although the matter has not yet surfaced, there are many who are secretly withering away because of this. Since society has no impetus to shift their minds to other areas, the sorrow they increase for no reason is truly unjust.

If we take a broader view, marriage is only a private matter between men and women, and society has no need to cheer, applaud, help, or join in the fun. If the enthusiasm, time, money, and energy used in this area are shifted to childcare centers, wouldn't the benefits to society be far greater? Moreover, this would shift the public's attention, making people know what to value and what to take lightly, and the future of the nation could also be freed from a layer of darkness; social morality and the anxiety of unmarried women could be greatly adjusted.

Such a Charitable Maternity Hospital 194

— Qian

——In the outpatient clinic——

It seems that as long as it is a person, everyone will say, "Giving birth to children is a woman's natural duty." But regardless of whether it is a natural duty or an earthly duty, people may say it is terribly important, but few people care about how to enable women to safely fulfill this duty. In recent years, although there have occasionally been people who have been baptized by science and who hold the rice bowl of obstetrics, shouting out on the newspapers that women must not be poisoned by traditional midwives again, and must go to maternity hospitals, no one has ever mentioned the extent of the equipment in maternity hospitals, the safety of maternity hospital deliveries for the lives of mothers and infants, and whether the treatment received by pregnant women in hospitals is sound.

Speaking of which, the few maternity hospitals and the situation inside that this article is going to mention are certainly not the places where wealthy old men spend hundreds or thousands of taels of silver to live (according to reliable sources, the wife of a certain mayor gave birth and hired the president of a certain large hospital to deliver the baby, and the delivery fee was one thousand taels of silver). On the contrary, since it is called "charitable," it is a place where wealthy people open the door of convenience for poor people. The charitable maternity hospitals mentioned here are all maternity departments in charitable hospitals with religious affiliations that imperialists use as a means of cultural invasion.

Although there are many relatively complete private maternity hospitals in Shanghai, the lack of economic power deprives poor pregnant women of the freedom to choose doctors and maternity hospitals, and some poor pregnant women's knowledge in their minds prevents them from trusting traditional midwives. Therefore, in the one or two months before giving birth, they have to brace their bulging bellies and settle on the last road—that is, to go to a charitable maternity hospital run by a religious organization to try their luck.

I am also one of the women who is about to fulfill her "natural duty," and this "natural duty" is the third time I am fulfilling it. The dangers and horrors I have experienced and seen in the past are now constantly reminding me to prepare for the third time as soon as possible. Like those of us who are often followed by thieves, although we have suffered great losses in charitable maternity hospitals, this time, we still have to knock on the door of heaven, hoping that God has a conscience and that the doctors and nurses I encounter are responsible and humane.

Just like that, I walked into one of the largest charitable hospitals in Shanghai at 8:30 in the morning, with a seven-month-old fetus in my belly like a kangaroo. After paying 300 cash for registration, it was already 9:30. Although the regulations clearly stipulate that the obstetrics and gynecology clinic hours are from 10:00 to 11:00 in the morning, the doctor's shadow had not been seen by 10:45. In a small waiting room crowded with big bellies and gynecological patients, there was also an old man carrying a large bag of strange books, preaching while selling them. He kept murmuring something like "The Kingdom of Heaven is near" and other nonsense. But it was really "The Kingdom of Heaven is near," because a great doctor walked into the examination room with an air of great importance, followed closely by a gorgeously dressed fashionable woman. Everyone's hearts and eyes suddenly lit up, thinking that they would be rescued immediately; who knew that about a quarter of an hour later, the great doctor and the fashionable woman walked out of the examination room one after the other with an air of great importance. At this time, a middle-aged woman who had been waiting for a long time at the door of the examination room suppressed her temper and asked the nurse in a low voice, "Miss, why doesn't the doctor see me? I'm number one." The nurse, with a face full of freckles and somewhat like a shrew, scolded disdainfully, "The doctor hasn't come yet, that's Doctor ×'s own patient, understand?"

Just as I was wondering what "the doctor's own patient" meant, a big belly next to me told me, "This Doctor × is a bastard. When I came to check my second child the year before last, I ran into him. He shamelessly took advantage of the nurse's absence and pinched my thigh. I gave him a good slap."

While we were talking like this, a few wealthy ladies walked in, each accompanied by several nanny-like people, followed by two female trainee doctors in uniforms. The noisy people gradually calmed down again, and everyone focused all their attention on the examination room.

Soon, the examination room really roared like a furnace that had added coal, but the first to be called in for examination were the nanny-like people brought by the wealthy ladies. After careful inquiries, I learned that they were all milkmaids who sold their blood for two dollars of special registration fee and five dollars of blood test fee paid by the ladies.

It had been going on until after twelve o'clock, and I was finally called into the examination room by the shrew-like nurse. It didn't take three minutes for a seven-month pregnant woman to be examined for the first time, and all the procedures were completed. When I walked out of the hospital door, I was still wondering. But there was one thing that I saw clearly; that was the urine that I was told to excrete for testing was in the same urinal, and a gynecological patient had also urinated on top of my urine. This perfunctory and irresponsible outpatient service immediately evoked the terrifying scenes I had seen in the maternity hospital before, and I really shuddered in the heat.

Short Story

Selling a Daughter 195

— Zhanquan

The river turned a bend, and the increasingly distant and delicate stern of the boat finally disappeared from sight. With a resentful gaze, she stared intently at the long stretch of undulating waves that had been broken by the boat's oars. It seemed as if she wanted to blame it for its dry belly during the summer, which had dried up the rice in the fields and ruined everyone's livelihood. Now, it was gurgling and carrying the boat away with her daughter, never to return. The inability to suppress and eliminate the anger in her belly made Shun Gu's mother begin to realize the childishness of this curse-like expression.

There was still little sound from the nearby houses. The door of her own house was ajar. In the open space in front of the door, a faint light of the early sun shone. When she thought of the lively scene of a pigtail-tugging, east-jumping, west-bouncing scene that would never reappear, her heart became even heavier and beyond words. She pushed the door in a daze and collapsed onto a broken chair in a daze; a burst of wailing that she could no longer hold back immediately shook the cold air in the small house and alarmed the kind-hearted people of the same fate in the neighborhood.

"Shun Gu was sent away today? ... Look on the bright side! There's not enough to wear or eat at home, but at least she'll survive outside. Moreover, thirty-odd dollars is not a small amount, and if you put a little more together, you can get through until the 'Chunhua' harvest. It's not good for the whole family to starve to death; and besides, you're finally paying off that rent you owe?"

"Yes, who isn't suffering these days? Didn't Sister A-Yu sell her clever A-Cui a few days ago? Old Man Bing also sold the sturdy ox that had been his companion for many years. Those who have no children or livestock are selling off everything they can't live without! Alas, what can we do!"

"Really, Heaven wants us to suffer, what can we say! Have you forgotten that Brother A-Liang picked out his newborn baby and exchanged it for a dollar? Raising her to seven or eight years old is enough to do her justice. We have no choice but to sell to save our own lives!"

"Alas, she's going to be a little nun! She hasn't even properly lived a day of her life, and she's being wrongly sent into the empty gate. Isn't that a living sin? When she grows up and understands things, she'll resent her parents for being so cruel. Poor thing, she really thought she was going to the provincial capital to play, and she was laughing and waving to me all the way on the bow of the boat!"

"Moreover, the more people who eat vegetarian food and chant Buddhist scriptures, the narrower their minds and the more ruthless their hearts. She might end up in a misfortune where she is beaten and scolded day and night. Wouldn't that really make Shun Gu suffer?"

The fat-headed and chubby-faced image floated into her mind, clearly, with a pair of bright and piercing eyes embedded in it. When the whole family went to the provincial capital to negotiate with the nunnery three days ago, the reason that made her most unwilling to make the deal was that the nun's appearance was outwardly kind but inwardly treacherous, and she was afraid that Shun Gu would not be able to endure her torment. However, for the sake of money, her mother-in-law agreed, her husband was willing, and she could only say a little more to learn more about the great principles of life. She helplessly waited for the coming of the living separation that was equivalent to death, and for several days, she had been inseparable from Shun Gu until this morning.

But now her hands were empty. When she thought that she would no longer be able to get that kind of innocent and lovely comfort in her spare time after work, a more intense heartache was accompanied by the memory of her youngest son who died in the spring of last year—because she had a fever after childbirth, dried up her milk, had no money to send her out to find milk, and couldn't afford any milk or soy milk, the infant, who was still very lacking in life skills, finally starved to death alive in half a month.

The low mourning, accompanied by sobs and narrations, turned into a fierce and tragic cry. This individual's cry encompassed the common suffering of the masses; this made her companions unable to help but sigh and wipe their tears frequently while repeatedly comforting her, each grieving for their own but universally the same fate.

However, time was not something they could waste at will, unlike some people; finally, everyone thought that they had to continue to fight with their own muscles and fate, hurriedly offered their last words of earnest persuasion, and successively went to do their own lives.

A series of messy but familiar footsteps stopped in front of the door. The wind quickly pushed open the half-closed firewood door, bringing in a ray of slanted sunlight that was still very strong. In the dazzling sunlight, who was jumping closer to her mother but Shun Gu, for whom she had been breaking her heart for several days and crying her eyes dry in the middle of the day?

Silence and surprise occupied a moment. Finally, with an annoyed tone, her husband told the story of the breakdown of the transaction as if he were angry at himself and complaining to someone

"What kind of compassion do these monks have! They clearly agreed on four dollars per year that day, for a total of thirty-two dollars. But today they went back on their word again, saying that heads are not worth much these days, that thirty-two dollars is too expensive, that cutting off the odd change would make it an even number, that they must pay the original price and they didn't want it, and said a lot of things. Despite our repeated pleas, kowtows, and prayers, and saying everything we could say, we couldn't move her heart at all. Later, she simply said that we had to pay the middleman's fee ourselves. This thief nun, who would have thought that she said these words on purpose; when I couldn't bear the anger and said that it would be better to make her a foster daughter, she eagerly said good, good, you can just go and make her a foster daughter, I won't force you. Get out quickly, get out of here immediately. Like chasing away beggars, that's how we left that thief nunnery."

Now, Shun Gu's mother clearly knew that her daughter was returning to her, and an unexpected and simple joy temporarily filled her whole body; she dared not express it, but could not suppress it, gently stroking her daughter's small hands and tidying up the messy hair on her head. But when she looked up, her eyes met her mother-in-law's gloomy face and her husband's angry gaze, and immediately, a dark shadow of fear of life enveloped her heart again.

"Damn it, what a clever idea someone came up with; selling one's own children to temporarily prolong a dog's miserable life! Can children be sold endlessly? Do people who don't have children not live? What about those of us who can't sell our daughters? Langfadi always says 'We should find a smarter and more meaningful way out,' and I'm just starting to understand a little now! I'm going to ask him for advice."

After saying these words, Shun Gu's master's back foot had already stepped outside the threshold.

Lecture on Women's Issues

Lecture 10 Historical Examination of Women's Liberation Thought 196

Section 1 Democratic Women's Liberation Thought

As we know, so-called democracy or liberalism is the most effective tool for the modern bourgeoisie to break the feudal autocracy. That is to say, when the bourgeoisie established a foundation on the ruins of the feudal society, it raised the banner of democracy and called on the oppressed masses under the feudal system. As a result, the oppressed women also bravely gathered into the democratic anti-feudal camp! In this way, they consciously began to demand equal rights for women and men in society. And in this way, the democratic women's liberation thought was formed.

This democratic liberation thought gave rise to so-called Feminism. Feminism can be translated as feminism or gender equality. Regarding its meaning, many people have different interpretations, but in general, it is to obtain equal rights with men under the capitalist social system. In other words, feminists do not oppose the existence of private property and class domination, but only oppose men's domination over women, do not want to change the current social system, but only demand equal rights with men, and only recognize the opposition between men and women, and deny the opposition of social classes. This kind of thought is essentially a product of bourgeois democracy or liberalism, and represents the thought of bourgeois women who were in the process of liberation at that time.

It can be said that the idea of ​​feminism originated from Rousseau's "Social Contract," but the "Declaration of Women's Rights" published by Gouges and Madame Roland during the French Revolution in the 18th century was the initial concrete performance of this thought. At the same time, in 1792, the British Ms. Wollstonecraft published the book "A Vindication of the Rights of Woman," which more specifically demanded equal rights for women and men in society. The prototype of feminism was completed and widely spread to European and American countries. Therefore, the world calls Wollstonecraft the originator of feminism.

Later, in the middle of the 19th century, with the establishment and development of bourgeois democratic regimes, feminist thought spread throughout European and American countries. The representative figures of this kind of thought can be regarded as John Stuart Mill in England, and Susan B. Anthony and Charlotte Perkins Gilman in the United States, and Ellen Key in Sweden. Their views on women are not consistent. For example, Mill was an enthusiastic advocate of women's suffrage. In his famous book "The Subjection of Women," he especially emphasized the legal status of women, that is, he mainly discussed the issue of women's liberation from a legal point of view. Susan B. Anthony wrote the book "Women and Labor," mainly explaining the liberation of women from the perspective of labor. Mrs. Gilman wrote the book "Women and Economics," mainly exploring the issue of women from an economic point of view. Finally, Ellen Key wrote books such as "The Century of the Child," "Love and Marriage," "The Women's Movement," and "The Rebirth of Motherhood," advocating the omnipotence of motherhood and the supremacy of love, and wanting to solve the problem of women from the perspective of both sexes. Due to space limitations, their specific opinions cannot be described in detail here, but in short, they are all feminists, and their thoughts are not unified. In other words, so-called feminist thought originally did not have any independent and unified system.

However. There is one point that should be paid special attention to here, that is, Ellen Key's views on love and motherhood are often maliciously used by people. She advocates protecting motherhood and advocating the unique freedom of motherhood, in order to freely choose love and marriage and fully develop the sexual ability of motherhood. He said: "All current efforts are preparing to create a better human race, which is the great driving force of passionate love. There is no such driving force other than love and parental love." In order to create a better human race, we must wait for the completion of motherhood, and women have the right to demand the completion of this motherhood, and society should of course bear this obligation. She advocates that women's natural duty is to be a wife and a mother, and opposes women engaging in labor outside the family or running around in political movements. She said:

"If women cannot get rid of the parasitic state of life from the past except by engaging in labor outside the family, then we would rather choose that kind of high-level life. Because of these two social evils, the latter is less harmful than the former."

Ellen Key's thought is contrary to the claims of general feminists. In detail, American feminists are against the parasitic life of being a wife and a mother, and advocate that women go deep into society and engage in the same activities as men. But from Ellen Key's point of view, this phenomenon is destroying the family, neglecting the great mission of women to be wives and mothers, and making the relationship between the two sexes a monetary transaction relationship without the so-called pure love marriage life. Therefore, Ellen Key especially emphasizes pure love and motherhood protection.

In short, feminist thought is a branch of bourgeois democratic thought. Although it does not have a certain unified system, it is consistent in opposing the abolition of private property and class struggle. This kind of thought has now completely lost its practical social significance.

Hysteria in the Nervous System 206

— Physician Feng Shanliang

Here, I can only describe the common symptoms of various different conditions, which are now called Hysteria Diathesis. The characteristics and reactions of hysteria, in the area of ​​perception, have (A) numbness, mostly in the entire or half side of the body, including the mucous membrane, or a segment of a limb. Many have narrowed visual fields, and there are often those with blindness, deafness, and loss of taste and smell. (B) Hypersensitivity in various skin areas, the stimulation of which can sometimes cause convulsive attacks. (C) Pain, headache, back pain, stomach pain, neuralgia of various nerves and joints. (D) All kinds of perceptual abnormalities, abnormal sensations in the internal organs, globus hystericus, ovarian sensations, etc. The most important thing in practice is the following fact: a severe hysterical state can also be caused by trauma, such as occupational injury, traumatic neurasthenia, injury, and war neurasthenia. However, this kind of neurasthenia is not caused by trauma. Its cause is the associated emotions, such as horror, anxiety, etc. Usually, the period between the injury and the initial onset of the illness is a week or several days. The injured person may begin to feel tired, various pains, dizziness, poor sleep, and weakness in the limbs after returning to work, leading to a state of neurasthenia. Weight loss occurs because there is often no major change that can be proven at the site of the illness, and patients are very easily suspected of faking the illness. Therefore, when diagnosing this type of nervous system condition, a precise and detailed examination must be performed to find the correct source of the illness before treatment.
