Current Affairs Research

The Question of British-French Cooperation 207

— Xi Ru

Every shot fired in East Africa shakes the soul of the British Empire. This is because if Italy defeats Abyssinia, not only will Britain's colonies in Africa feel a direct threat, but its sea route from the Mediterranean to the Far East will also be liable to be cut off at any time, thus endangering the disintegration of the British Empire. Therefore, since the sound of Mussolini's first shot towards Africa was heard, the atmosphere in London has been particularly tense. In addition to continuing to deploy defenses in the Mediterranean, the British government has also intensified its activities in Geneva, demanding that the League of Nations resolve to recognize Italy as an aggressor and impose sanctions on it. However, to deal with Italy effectively, Britain does not dare to take risks alone under the current situation. At the very least, it must have the considerable understanding of France before it dares to take action. Therefore, since the East Africa incident, Eden has been running between Paris, London, and Geneva, asking the French to support its sanctions against Italy, and the voices of British-French cooperation have become increasingly louder.

Originally, British and French diplomacy both used the League of Nations to enhance their own importance. But at present, Britain's attention is focused on the Mediterranean, while France is focused on the Rhine. Therefore, when Britain asked France to sanction Italy, France asked Britain whether it would impose the same sanctions on aggressors in Central Europe in the future; when Britain asked for French naval assistance in the Mediterranean, France also asked for the cooperation of the British army, navy, and air force. In this bargaining negotiation, Britain and France have gained considerable understanding and are gradually approaching each other. Now, the League of Nations has passed a resolution on sanctions against Italy, France has responded to the issue of naval aid to Britain, and the Italian-Ethiopian armistice negotiations are also underway, so some overly optimistic people say that the dawn of peace has appeared and the war may be avoided.

Indeed, British-French relations have a major role to play in the question of war and peace; if Britain and France can really cooperate and unanimously oppress Mussolini, it may be possible to make Italy "stop at the right time." But judging from the current situation, it can be said that Britain and France have gained considerable understanding on certain points; to say that Britain and France have thoroughly cooperated is a premature judgment. We believe that Britain and France can only be consistent in maintaining the existence of the League of Nations and in maintaining the temporary stability of Europe, so France can only try to make Italy "stop at the right time," and Britain can only be responsible to France on general security issues. It is very difficult when it comes to truly jointly confronting Italy or jointly confronting Germany. Because it is not easy for Britain to completely sacrifice the British-German understanding gained from the London Naval Treaty, and it is not easy for France to tear up the French-Italian Rome Agreement on its own. In fact, the recent replies from France and Britain only stated that if the British navy suffers an unreasonable attack from the Italian navy, the French navy can provide assistance; on the other hand, if the British navy wants to attack Italy and implement military sanctions, then it is a problem in France. As for the issue of sanctions, France only stated that it agreed to implement economic sanctions, but "has not considered" issues such as blockading the Suez Canal or blockading Italian ports. Similarly, London has not made a concrete response to France's request for joint defense against Germany. The recent statements made by British Prime Minister Baldwin and Foreign Minister Hoare are also some empty talk of "maintaining the alliance" and "maintaining peace," and have not made any concrete expressions regarding France's request. In Hoare's speech, there was a passage worth pondering: "The great experiment we are currently conducting is unprecedented in the world for generations. The collective security mechanism is now being implemented for the first time. If the experiment is successful, we will not find it difficult to sit back and watch its effectiveness; if the experiment is unsuccessful, then all those who advocate not using war as a national tool will suffer a major blow of disappointment. If this experiment fails, then those who participate in the action with a wavering attitude should bear a major responsibility. ...Who is faithfully upholding the collective security system, and who is shouting high to uphold the collective security system, but attacking and provoking the countries that implement collective security? We can almost identify them." The implication is already obvious. - From this we can say that under the current situation, the so-called British-French cooperation is limited.

Naturally, even such limited British-French cooperation has a great influence on the European situation. It is very clear that due to France's participation in economic sanctions and its conditional naval assistance to the British in the Mediterranean, Mussolini feels that the situation is not very certain. Although the effectiveness of the so-called economic sanctions is limited because Japan, the United States, and Germany stand outside the League of Nations and because the interests of European countries are different, Italy has lost more than 130 million lire in its expedition to East Africa, and its economic and political crisis is developing. Under this circumstance, even the economic sanctions that Britain and France can do are a major blow to it. Therefore, Mussolini is conducting military and diplomatic activities at the same time at this time, preparing for war on the one hand and proposing ceasefire conditions for negotiations on the other, in order to ease the situation. According to general observation, if British-French cooperation can continue to develop, then the conditions proposed by Italy may gradually decrease, so the East African issue may be temporarily resolved. Such a possibility certainly exists. However, this possibility will not become a reality in a short period of time; if the time for resolving the issue is extended to several months or a year, then night will be long and dreams will be many, and the results will still be unpredictable.

To go a step further, even if Britain and France can cooperate further, the European situation cannot be estimated simply and optimistically. First, France and the Soviet Union are now very friendly, while Britain has always been the organizer of the anti-Soviet front. If Britain and France cooperate further, it is a big question whether Britain will become friendly with the Soviet Union as a result. Britain's pulling of France does not necessarily mean that it wants to be close to Russia, and Britain's toleration of Italy does not necessarily mean that it wants to oppose Germany; similarly, France's cooperation with Britain does not necessarily mean that it wants to oppose Italy or even Russia, and it certainly does not necessarily mean that it wants to be close to Germany; they all have their own hidden intentions even in their cooperation. What Britain wants is to use France to ease the conflict between Britain and Italy, to strive to mediate the contradictions between France and Germany, and to incite Germany to advance eastward; France's attempt is to unite Britain while also pulling in the Soviet Union and Italy to defend against Germany, but these two attempts are clearly in conflict. Second, if Britain and France can cooperate further, it will inevitably prompt Germany and Italy to join hands, thereby further forming a combination of Germany, Italy, Austria, Hungary, and Poland, becoming a new group force in Europe. At that time, it is also quite questionable whether Britain, France, and even the Soviet Union can unite as they did before the war and confront Germany, Italy, etc., replaying the tragedy that occurred in 1914. Therefore, third, even if Britain and France can cooperate further, its future is still difficult to say; and the changes in the European situation still cannot be concluded simply.

But no matter what, we can say that the crisis of the Second World War is still very great; moreover, no one can say how long it will take for this crisis to become a reality. Judging from the current situation, the Italian-Ethiopian issue cannot be resolved in the short term; even if Britain and France can cooperate within a certain limit to force Italy to "stop at the right time" so that the East African issue can be temporarily eased or temporarily resolved, the war will soon break out in other places and on other issues. In Austria, in the Baltic Sea, in the Balkans, in the Far East, ... the world is full of gunpowder! When the last World War was about to break out, the great powers were desperately expanding their military equipment, so someone asked at that time: Who are those weapons used to target? Now the military equipment of the great powers is many times higher in quality than during the last World War. At this time, can you not raise the question of who those weapons are used to target?

Outlying Postal Agency

The Miao People's "Drum-Pulling Festival" 208

— Zu'an

Correspondence from Rong County, Guangxi

The Miao and Yi people, who live scattered across the provinces of Yunnan, Guizhou, and Guangxi, hold so many various grand ceremonies to worship gods each year that it would be impossible to list them all. However, the absurd and preposterous nature of these ceremonies is largely the same. The Miao people's "Drum-Pulling Festival" discussed here is one of the most important and exceptionally absurd of these sacred gatherings.

The Drum-Pulling Festival is the most important of all the Miao people's sacred gatherings, and its rituals are more solemn and grand than those of other such gatherings. The expenses required are also enormous, often requiring the pooled wealth of an entire Miao clan or a significant portion thereof to stage this grand celebration. To us, this may seem like a foolish act that is absurd, pointless, wasteful, and mentally exhausting. However, they believe it is related to the prosperity and decline of the race and the abundance of the harvest. Even if they are so poor that they struggle to feed themselves, they still hold it on schedule. From this, we can imagine that what dominates the consciousness of the Miao people is not the science of the 20th century, but divine authority.

Although the cost of holding the "Drum-Pulling Festival" is enormous, fortunately, it only occurs once every thirteen years, with the period for each festival usually around November of the year. When the festival is approaching, enthusiastic elder Miao people from various villages prepare everything, procuring pigs, cattle, and food. Each festival requires anywhere from a dozen to dozens of pigs and cattle. Even if a particular village lacks the financial resources to prepare such a large offering, the villagers must tighten their belts and painfully sacrifice in order to wish for a bountiful year. On the first day of the grand festival, two leaders are publicly elected from each village, along with a dozen or so wealthy individuals to lead the ceremony. Each leader must offer twelve or thirteen aquatic creatures, while the wealthy individuals offer one each, or several contribute to one. Once all preparatory procedures are completed, the elder Miao people in charge of preparations notify each village of the date to attend the ceremony.

On the day of the grand festival, a spacious sandy flat area is found by a river. There, a bed is set up, with the surroundings completely covered with hanging paintings of various animals such as fish, crows, insects, and mice, arranged like a shrine in a temple. At this time, the wealthiest person who offered the most sacrifices lies down on the bed, face up, eyes tightly closed, holding their breath silently like a dead person, not allowed to twitch in the slightest. The crowd then believes they are the incarnation of the "Black Dog"—Note: explained later—and roars with joy, slaughtering cattle and pigs, burning incense, and celebrating. All the raw meat sacrifices and the misty incense smoke surround the pseudo-dead person—the wealthy individual—and thousands of people breathe on them. However, the wealthy individual, even in such an environment, is not allowed to move even once.

After the crowd completes the sacrifices, they take a "Dou Fei Yao" tree—Note: transliteration of the Miao language, details below—which can be several dozen or several feet long, depending on the size of the crowd. They hollow out the center of the tree and pass a thick, sturdy rope through it, tying countless smaller ropes to both ends. Every participating member of the crowd, regardless of age or gender, holds one of these ropes and pulls against each other. The scene resembles construction workers in the interior driving piles. Both ends pull back and forth, and they shout loudly in unison, filling the entire venue with a crazed atmosphere. This is a scene of "Drum-Pulling." While "Drum-Pulling" is in progress, two or three hundred people play the "Lusheng" to add to the excitement, spending the whole day from morning to night in a mood of joy and exhilaration. However, the one suffering is the wealthy individual. While the crowd is celebrating at the peak of excitement, they must remain motionless like a dead person; otherwise, the "Drum-Pulling" upon which the rise and fall of the race depends will fail, and the lives of all the Miao people will be in grave danger!

Thus, until dusk, when everyone feels tired and hungry after excessive excitement, the "Drum-Pulling" is declared over. Everyone gathers in front of the god—the wealthy individual—to cook and eat the pork and beef, and the remainder is divided and distributed to everyone by the next wealthiest person to take back home. As for the wealthy individual who played dead, they can only get up from the bed and go back to eat something after the crowd has left. By the time the three-day ritual ceremony is over, this wealthy individual who played dead, even if they do not die, will suffer a major illness. It is even common for someone to actually die from playing dead. Although this behavior is foolish, the selected wealthy individual does not refuse because they believe that dying on the bed like this is to be assimilated with the gods, which is an honor they could not wish for more!

After the three days of the "Drum-Pulling Festival" are over, all participating members of the crowd visit each other's homes to offer congratulations, celebrating the attainment of wealth and happiness. The hosts slaughter pigs and cattle, inviting the guests to eat and drink to their hearts' content for several days. Generally, young men and women are usually prevented from getting close to each other due to the restrictions of etiquette, but during these few days, they can openly perform their comedy. Even if parents see it, they do not blame them, and sometimes even help to make it happen. Therefore, the young men and women of the Miao people greatly hope that the "Drum-Pulling Festival" will be held frequently, so that they can complete their good deeds. It is only a pity that it can only be held once every thirteen years, which they cannot help but consider a regrettable thing!

The thirtieth day after the "Drum-Pulling Festival" is called "Full Moon." On this day, the Miao people from each village piously carry the "Dou Fei Yao" tree up the mountain, hold a ceremony of worship and reverence, and then the entire sacred ceremony is considered complete.

Speaking of the origin of this "Drum-Pulling Festival," it is simply a mythological story. According to a Miao person, "There was once a Tang king who had several daughters. Among them, the second daughter was the most beautiful and virtuous, so the Tang king loved her especially. After a few years, these daughters grew up and married one after another. Only the second daughter remained by his side because the Tang king loved her.

Once, bandits invaded the territory, and the Tang king was defeated. He immediately packed up his property and led his family to flee overseas. However, due to the haste of departure, he forgot to bring out a national jade seal. From then on, the Tang king was depressed and unhappy all day long, and he was very distressed, always thinking about the jade seal. Later, one day, he met Yama, and he asked Yama to find a way to retrieve the jade seal, but Yama could not think of a way either. The two people were speechless and pondered silently for a long time. Later, he came up with an idea himself and told Yama, "I want to post a reward. If anyone can cross the sea and retrieve my jade seal, no matter what kind of person they are, or even if they are a pig or a dog, they can be matched with my daughter."

Yama did not say a word after hearing this, but just glanced at him sideways. Unexpectedly, a black dog that Yama had brought along heard his words and decided to retrieve the jade seal in order to marry that beautiful woman. Sure enough, after Yama led it back, it did not reveal a word. It went straight to the sea with a wooden stick several feet long in its mouth. It floated in the sea for a few days and spent a lot of effort before finally reaching the shore. When it looked up, it only saw that the old capital of the Tang king still housed many bandits. It thought to itself: this time, the jade seal can only be retrieved by wisdom, not by force. It first started by contacting similar creatures and building emotional connections. It followed them around all day long, and after a long time, their feelings gradually merged. The palace of the Tang king was also memorized in its stomach because they guided it.

One day, it invited several companions to go to the palace of the Tang king, wandering around secretly to find the place where the jade seal was stored. It offered food to its companions to eat when it encountered it. The general bandits treated it like an ordinary dog, and did not mind letting it walk around freely. Thus, until it got dark, it suddenly saw a strong light shining on a large table, illuminating the entire room. Its heart could not help but move, and it walked towards the light. When it reached the front, it saw that it was indeed the jade seal that the Tang king was thinking about. It was overjoyed for a moment, and secretly crouched under the table, holding its breath silently for several hours. When it looked around, it saw that the bandits were all asleep. It suddenly jumped onto the table, held the jade seal in its mouth, and quietly slipped out of the bandits' area.

A few days later, it safely crossed the sea and delivered the jade seal to the Tang king. The Tang king looked down and was immediately shocked speechless. At this time, Yama also came after hearing the news and congratulated the Tang king. However, the Tang king was filled with mixed feelings of joy and worry, and could not think of an idea for a while. Later, his second daughter heard the news and hurried over to relieve her father's pain, agreeing to the reward offered by her father in one breath.

After she married the black dog, the Tang king gave her a few acres of land and told her to plant trees to make a living. The black dog lay by her side during the day and slept with her like a couple at night. After a year, she actually gave birth to a child. The Tang king was overjoyed when he heard the news and sent people to send many axes and more than a hundred bundles of grain stalks (the Miao people bundle grain ears, each bundle weighing about three or four pounds) as gifts. From then on, they lived a carefree life more joyfully. However, good times do not last forever, and eventually it became their mockery! One day, suddenly many people brought a lot of hunting dogs to hunt on the mountain near their home. The sound of dogs barking echoed through the valleys. The black dog was deeply moved by the sound of the hunting dogs, and followed them to hunt on the mountain. Unexpectedly, when it walked to a steep cliff, it suddenly lost its footing and fell down. Coincidentally, a "Dou Fei Yao" tree grew in the middle of the cliff, and the black dog was hung on this tree stump.

The Tang king's second daughter knew that it was unlikely to return when it had left and that its misfortune was great. She had no way to find out where it was, and she was unspeakably sad. The Miao people in the nearby area heard the unfortunate news and felt sorry for her!

After the black dog died, due to her diligent operation, the family became more prosperous day by day, and her son grew up day by day. The mother and son lived a peaceful life. One day, the son remembered his father's tragic death, so he went to the valley where his father had "hunted" to find its remains. After working hard for a few days, he finally found a pair of bright red bones of his father in a tree stump in the cliff. This strange news immediately spread throughout the Miao people's villages. Everyone believed that these bones could not rot and that its son could make a fortune because of the spirituality of this "Dou Fei Yao" tree. Therefore, the general Miao people competed to risk their lives to cut down the tree and carry it back, hollow out the center of the tree, and put it on a rope, offering it like a god. Coincidentally, the year its son found its remains was exactly thirteen years old, so the general Miao people hold a "Drum-Pulling Festival" once every thirteen years.

Needless to say, this story is absurd and magical, but the motivation of the general Miao people to hold this meeting is still inseparable from the idea of "getting rich," just like the ideas held by civilized people!

Amateur Study

The Question of Amateur Foreign Language Learning 209

— Qu Jia

I remember that last year this newspaper published an article on the question of "whether to learn a foreign language in one's spare time." At that time, it was not ignored by me, a young shop assistant who lacked spare time but had a strong desire to read. Because there was more than one article published, and the opinions were different, it was quite difficult for me to adapt for a while. First of all, I accepted the editor's opinion and decided to read some basic knowledge books first, and abandon foreign languages. The results were good. However, when I seemed to have acquired some basic knowledge, I immediately realized that the knowledge I had acquired was too shallow and felt that future progress would be very slow. It should be stated that this is not because I am old and my mind is wandering. It is just that the subject I am studying is social science. Knowing some scientific theories without examples to illustrate them is like reading dead books. What is the use of accumulating without transforming? At that time, I turned around and wanted to learn a foreign language. I think English is more common. If I can read foreign magazines and newspapers, I can also know more about world affairs. I had encountered English in elementary school before, and I knew it was difficult. But when I thought of the saying that "the word 'difficult' only exists in the dictionary of fools," I was courageous and determined. From then on, I studied hard and kept chanting in my mouth. Unexpectedly, after half a year of study, no results were seen. At that time, I thought of learning Esperanto. However, some friends thought that I was "fickle" and that I would end up achieving nothing. But within three months, I actually made rapid progress. I think this should be attributed to the simplicity and ease of learning Esperanto. If it cannot enable me to achieve the goal of reading magazines and newspapers, it is possible to give up halfway.

In the past, I did not know such a small place as Saar. Later, I read a Saar newsletter in an Esperanto magazine and learned about its geographical location and its importance. When the Saar region voted.

Page 19

The content of the Saar issue was published in Chinese newspapers. At that time, it could only be regarded as old news for me. Recently, Chinese newspapers have published war news about Italy and Abyssinia for days, but I know it in more detail in the Esperanto newsletter. Regarding cultural news, such as when I saw in the Shen Bao and Da Wan Bao that "the 27th International Esperanto Congress will be held in Rome in August, and the Chinese Ministry of Education has sent a representative from the embassy in Italy to participate nearby, and Mussolini will serve as the temporary chairman at that time," this matter is related to world affairs, so please forgive me for knowing it long ago. Moreover, not only that, because the Chinese newspapers did not mention the grand event of traveling to Africa! All this proves that Esperanto news is well-informed, but what does it reveal to people?

The "difficulty" of English certainly makes people a "fool." Now, grasping a beautiful and easy-to-learn language will no longer allow me to be called "fickle" and "change my mind." If learning Esperanto is easy is "easy to do," and knowing that learning Esperanto is so easy is so useful is "difficult to know," I am willing to let everyone know this hard-won thing together.

Art Scene

Review of "City Scenery" 210

— Mingyao

There is no question that "City Scenery" stands out from domestic films with a brand-new attitude. Not only does the choreography adopt new methods and techniques, but it also "uses music to describe the movements, psychological changes, and scene transitions of the characters in the play." It is a so-called "new type of musical drama" that creates a unique style.

Domestic sound films have made considerable progress, but due to their short history, they have only achieved achievements in dialogue or songs at most. There is no talk of "musical masterpieces," let alone "sound and shadow art"! However, film art must be urged to progress in order to describe the complex social environment and meet the needs of the audience. This time, the Diantong Company has created this new type of musical drama with an experimental attitude. This spirit of courage and effort is admirable.

Now, for the sake of clarity, I will briefly introduce the story as follows:

"At a small station in a certain village, farmers abandon their farm tools and flock to Shanghai. While waiting for the train, a person playing with a peep show (played by Yuan Muzhi) sings and solicits business. So, a family of four, father, mother, daughter, and nephew, go to watch. The peep show shows "City Scenery": Li Menghua (played by Tang Na), a young man in the city, is a penniless "unknown writer," but he is in love with Zhang Xiaoyun (played by Zhang Xinzhu), a fashionable lady who is not well-off but loves to dress up. Zhang also has a lover, Wang Junshan (played by Gu Menghe), a tea shop manager with some wealth who usually likes to play with women and pretends to be阔. The daughter's father (played by Zhou Boxun) is one of the shareholders of the pawnshop, and the family's finances are very tight, so he often asks the pawnshop for money, but the pawnshop's business is not good, so he is repeatedly rejected. In the end, he even takes the things pawned by others home to use for the New Year. Later, Li Menghua was defeated by money, and Xiaoyun was taken away by Junshan. However, because Junshan usually pretends to be wealthy, he spends a lot of money, and his business loses money. Before the end of the year, creditors come to the door to urge him to pay, so he abandons Xiaoyun and quietly flees. When Xiaoyun and her father find out and chase to the station, the train has already left. The "City Scenery" in the peep show ends here. The father, mother, daughter, and nephew who watched the peep show turn their heads and remember that they are rushing to Shanghai by train. At this time, two trains are about to leave separately, but they do not know what to do. As a result, both trains leave in their panic!"

The story is very simple, almost entirely love. In fact, it can be said that the whole play is a clue of several improper men and women entangled. Just because of the new techniques of description, it appears fresh and lively. In addition, the music helps to describe the movements and psychological changes of the characters in the play, making it feel more relaxed and cheerful. There is no question that "City Scenery" is a slapstick comedy. After watching it, you can indeed "laugh from beginning to end," but it is not like the "slapstick films" of the past that are fabricated, pretentious, and slapstick. It grabs reality as the theme and portrays it from the opposite side using a humorous satirical method. For example, the awkward appearance of the peep show player when he first appears evokes your laughter, but when he starts singing a business song in a hoarse voice, your "laughter" is stained with a sour tone. For example, the four people who watched the peep show showed a flustered attitude of pulling east and west when the train was about to leave, which made people laugh, but when they thought that these men and women had left the countryside and could not insert themselves into the sinful city, the situation of "not knowing what to do" made people feel a sour taste in their hearts!

The playwright gives the meaning of "City Scenery" to expose the sins and ugliness in the city. Therefore, there are charming vixen who sell wind and ride modernly (Zhang Xiaoyun), young evil people in foreign venues who play with women and pretend to be rich (Wang Junshan), flatterers and lackeys (Wang Junshan's secretary, Secretary Chen), and intellectual youths who do not seek progress and regard love as the supreme doctrine (Li Menghua...). These types of people are common in the city. The playwright grabs these types of people and makes powerful satire and ridicule. Therefore, "love supremacists" are eventually kicked away by others, "empty shele builders" eventually collapse, and fashionable ladies who envy vanity end up in a desolate situation. Among them, the "love supremacists" are especially subjected to harsh ridicule: Li Menghua, a poor writer with no reputation and no money, does not seek progress from the road he takes, but insists on love as a routine, and also pursues a vain modern woman. Therefore, there are various embarrassing situations such as owing rent to buy decorations for his lover, pawning his watch into the dance hall, and mistakenly giving the pawn ticket as a admission ticket. It is really full of jokes and ugly appearances. This divine satire is justified, and Chu is very reasonable.

These are all the sins and ugliness of the city, but its appearance is very impressive, just like the peep show cannot be debunked. The playwright uses this "peep show" to see through the various forms in the "City Scenery." The use of techniques can be said to be very flexible. When the eyes of the four people waiting for the train come into contact with the peep show, the towering buildings in the city, the roaring cars, ... all clearly slip past their eyes, as if it is a very grand and lively paradise. However, the last contact is the cave of sin. All the ugly people are active there, so the fantasy of the city is lost.

The entire plot is very tight, and it can consistently grasp the emotions of the audience. From beginning to end, they want to laugh, want to laugh, smile, and laugh loudly. At the same time, because of the music that is arranged to suit the plot, it adds a lot of power. This is where the "new type of musical drama" is superior to other "slapstick films" or "popular films."

However, "City Scenery" cannot be considered a completely successful work. We must know that the ugliness in the city cannot be represented by those few small clowns. The playwright only takes these few small characters to ridicule as much as possible, and ignores the big sins and the people who create sins. Even the petty officials (Wang Junshan), lackeys (Secretary Chen), and vixen (Zhang Xiaoyun) among those few small characters are lightly let go, and the poor writers are regarded as the main targets of ridicule. It has to be said that the playwright's eyes only see the small things, and let go of the big aspects. At the same time, the father, mother, daughter, and nephew who watch the peep show are the father, mother, and daughter in the "City Scenery" shown in the mirror, but the nephew becomes the "love supremacist" Li Menghua. I don't know why one person has to play two roles? If the playwright's intention is to imply that the types of people in "City Scenery" are the faces of the peep show watchers in the city, then that is a mistake. Because these farmers who "abandon their farm tools" always have unavoidable hardships before they leave the countryside and wander to the city. No matter how the urban environment changes their lives and temperaments, they are not qualified to be "vixens" or "love supremacists"... On the contrary, they have to desperately pursue work and struggle and groan painfully on the lifeline!

In addition to the distortion of the theme, the arrangement of actors is not very appropriate. Zhang Xinzhu, as the heroine, seems to have nothing to commend. Her expressions and movements are very stiff, and her lines are not very proficient. Originally, she should have many places to "act." As a woman who admires vanity, she has to deal with two lovers, please her parents, and also plan for her own expenses. She needs a lively posture, smooth communication, gentle movements, and flirtatious expressions to suit her situation. However, she has not exerted these kinds of personality abilities! Tang Na, as the male lead, is also very ordinary. A "love supremacist" should show a very enthusiastic attitude towards his lover, and especially show extreme regret and even cry and go crazy after losing love, but Tang Na did not do this. Although the sad performance can destroy the atmosphere of the comedy, crying can also add to the laughter! What is worth praising is Gu Menghe and Lan Ping. They are very competent for the roles they play. Their expressions and movements are also very realistic and not forced. It is a pity that they have too few opportunities to "act." If they were changed into the main characters, they might add a lot of color to the whole play!

In short, "City Scenery" has many shortcomings, but it cannot hide its advantages. Its new appearance is worth seeing.

Book and Newspaper Introduction

Introduction to "Life Knowledge" 211

— Bao

— Priced at eight cents per copy, sold by the Public Magazine Company —

Amidst the clamor of "Magazine Year," "Tabloid Year," and "Economic Downturn," we have unfortunately witnessed the cessation of many good magazines (such as the renovated "Modern," and "Translation"...), but at the same time, many new publications have appeared before our eyes. This not only demonstrates the arduous struggle of those generally dedicated to the cultural movement, but also reveals the general public's urgent demand for new knowledge.

"Life Knowledge" is one such noteworthy publication among the many newly released. In its "Publishing Declaration," this publication, after stating the objective circumstances of its emergence, made the following self-description:

"Precisely because our publication is passively called forth by objective circumstances, we must, in accordance with objective circumstances, automatically establish a clear goal for our publication from a subjective perspective. The goal of our publication, as indicated by its name, is life knowledge. But not the knowledge that natural persons living at any time and in any place should possess, but rather the knowledge specific to modern Chinese society, where the national territory is being lost, the countryside is bankrupt, and 'natural disasters' are exacerbated by man-made calamities."

We have to say that the content of the publication is consistent with the stated goal in its "Publishing Declaration," although some aspects still do not entirely satisfy individuals.

Judging by the inaugural issue, "Life Knowledge" is a small, comprehensive cultural magazine. It contains writings on economics, politics, science, philosophy, and literature and art, all of which can generally be said to be written under the "goal" proposed in its "Publishing Declaration." Now, for the sake of clarity for readers, we will provide a brief introduction to the content of each section—

Regarding economic analysis, the inaugural issue contains two articles: Xu Xingjun's "The General Trend of the Modern World Economy" and Chu Xinjun's "What is Rose Doing in China?" The former first points out that the combination of monopoly and competition is the "root of the modern world's economic chaos"; then, based on this, it explains the emergence of "consolidation policies" and "tariff wars and currency wars" in foreign trade, resulting in the form of "economic nationalism"; subsequently, it further points out several new phenomena exhibited by the modern world economy under the prevalence of "economic nationalism": the disintegration of the international market, the reduction of the international division of labor, the increase of state intervention in economic life, and the lack of signs of a resolution to the chronic mass unemployment phenomenon. Finally, it points out the desire of various capitalist countries to use war as a way out of the world economic chaos. In a short article of four or five thousand words, the actual situation of the current world economy is clearly presented, which is the main feature of this article. The latter—"What is Rose Doing in China?"—explains the conflicts between Britain, Japan, and the United States in China from the perspective of Rose's visit to China. This is an article most closely related to our real life and is worth reading.

There are also two articles on international politics. The first is He Dui's "The Italian-Abyssinian War—Imperialist War—Peace," in which the author, based on recent facts, points out the reality of imperialist powers carving up Abyssinia and oppressing weak nations, and, based on the actual situation in Italy and the conflict between Britain and Italy, explains the causes of the East African issue. Finally, it concludes that in the conflict of imperialism, all weak nations must rise up "to resolve the conflicts between imperialists by resolving their own suffering." The second is Ling Junjun's "Several Prospects Estimated for the Italian-Abyssinian Conflict." Judging from the current situation, although the author's estimates seem to be somewhat inconsistent with the facts, there are also some noteworthy opinions in his analysis.

In the philosophy section, Si Qi's "The Key Points of Idealism" is a popular and concise article. Here, the author provides a brief explanation of the cosmology, ontology, epistemology, and methodology of idealistic philosophy. General beginners in philosophy can obtain a brief systematic concept of idealism after reading it.

The two articles in the science section are both very interesting and meaningful. "The Story of Inventions" is a translation, which tells the story of an invention related to extinguishing a major fire triggered by an oil well fire, and discusses many things about inventions. Although this article is not yet finished, we can already understand the meaning of the so-called "collective inventors" in the Soviet Union and some principles of natural science after reading the already published part. The next is Shu Qian's "Starting from the Relationship between Mathematics and Our Lives," which seems like a rigid article, but because the author explains the problem based on actual life and finds simple examples from actual life to illustrate the relationship between mathematics and life, reading it not only does not feel "rigid," but also feels very interesting.

"Life Knowledge" gives more importance to literature and art. But strictly speaking, some of the writings on literature and art published in the inaugural issue cannot compare with the articles in other sections. First, such as Guan Lu's novel "Bankruptcy," although it writes about a real phenomenon of the current Chinese society in the decline of industry and commerce, the author's artistic expression is very inadequate, thus making people feel that this is not an artistically depicted novel, but a simple narration of a story. Second, Zhou Gangming's "How to Read Novels," although this article is not yet finished, we feel that if the unpublished part of this article is consistent with

Page 20

Page 21

the published part, and written under the author's theoretical and writing skills, then this will be a relatively ordinary article lacking brilliance. Although what the author is talking about here is not theoretically problematic, it is just some empty theoretical principles that almost everyone knows, so it makes people feel that it lacks practical content and profound theory. I think the current readers have made some progress. They are already familiar with theoretical principles such as "literature is a social phenomenon" and "literature reflects social life." Therefore, our current responsibility is not to talk to them about theoretical principles in an empty way, but to actually apply the principles, develop the principles, and make our theory profound, substantial, and useful, so as not to become ordinary. Naturally, being popular is necessary, but wouldn't it be better if we could express profound theories in a popular form using practical materials and a lively and generous writing style? If being popular leads to being ordinary, isn't it as bad as not being popular? We hope that the editors and authors of "Life Knowledge" will pay special attention to this. In addition, Li Sheng's "About Mona Lisa," Zhang Geng's "Drama Lectures for the Audience," and Hou Mo's "Peach Blossom Fan" review are all works worth reading.

"Life Knowledge" still talks less about the general social phenomena currently occurring, thus reducing its realistic activeness. I think "Life Knowledge" should add a column dedicated to discussing the noteworthy social phenomena of reality, such as the "Social Phase" of "Reading Life" and the "Lookout" of "World Knowledge" (talking about international events). At the same time, although "Life Knowledge" has already achieved the popularity and mass appeal of the writing, we still hope that it will make more efforts in the depth of theory and the richness of content. Also, there are too many typos in this issue, and we hope that you will pay attention to proofreading in the future.

Miscellaneous Writings

Scattered Notes While Sick 212

— Xiao Ping

A body that was originally weak from birth has been placed in a job that requires a strong physique to deal with on a daily basis. Therefore, illness has become entangled with me.

In fact, it is just a minor illness, but it has caused me to be bedridden; my waist and limbs are sore, my head hurts in waves, and a slight breeze will make my whole body tremble. Everyone says, "Get a good night's sleep, sweat a lot, and you will be refreshed tomorrow." I thought so too, so I slept well in bed.

Sweat seeped out of my pores, and I was overjoyed. Afterwards, sweat poured out from all parts of my body like a flood. The sweat beads on my forehead were as large as beans. The smell of sweat wafted from the quilt into my nostrils in waves. It was really unbearably smelly. After enduring for some time, the quilt was almost like a damp bucket during the plum rain season. I really couldn't bear it anymore. I thought: Sweating this much is probably enough, so I boldly loosened the quilt.

Because I mostly drank boiled water, although I sweated, I still had to urinate, and it seemed that my bowel movement at 7 pm every night was also on time, so I wanted to go to the latrine. I am a single person and have always lived in the school dormitory. Because I live in the school, I have to abide by the various rules that general students must abide by. I can usually live this mechanical life, but I often suffer when I am sick, such as having a bowel movement, whether you are sick or not, you have to walk across a large square to get to the latrine. Because I was afraid of catching a cold while I was sick, I wrapped my whole body in a thick blanket. As soon as I staggered out of the dormitory, a cold wind hit me in the face, making me shiver all over. When I got to the latrine, I was dizzy and the world was spinning. It was hard to finish it in a daze and walk across the square back to the dormitory.

When I went back to bed, the residual warmth in the quilt was still there, which was much more comfortable. However, this night's sleep was really the most painful. I woke up in a fright from time to time in my dream, which was a very uncomfortable awakening.

I woke up earlier than usual the next day. I looked at the skylight and felt too uncomfortable to sleep in bed. I always thought that my minor illness must have been cured after a night's sleep, so I got dressed and washed up, but my head was swollen and painful, even more so than yesterday afternoon. I still went to class and asked the students to write compositions. I sat at the table and watched them carefully conceive their ideas. The dizziness in my head became even worse. I thought about letting them write their compositions well, and I could go back to the dormitory and lie down for a while. But then I thought, it's still not good, wouldn't it be boring to lie in the dormitory alone? And maybe if I don't accompany them, they will just do it sloppily and perfunctorily. Okay, let's just endure it!

In the afternoon, I still lay in bed, sweating large beads in the quilt, and fell asleep several times, half awake and half drowsy. I began to feel anxious: Could it turn into a serious illness?

Eating porridge had no taste, so I asked the tea room to send a can of corned beef from under the bed to the kitchen to steam and eat. Eating it also had no taste. After eating three pieces, my stomach inexplicably became uncomfortable after sleeping for a while. Finally, I vomited it out, and the strands of meat were still strands of meat.

At this time, I was hoping that there was some magical medicine that could immediately cure my illness. I didn't bother to worry about the pain of being sick, but I couldn't do many things that needed to be done urgently, and I couldn't meet friends who needed to be met urgently. Anxious, anxious, I have always been an impatient person, and I am even more anxious when I am sick.

Mr. Lu advised me to buy Tiger Balm and apply it to my temples. I did as he said. Mr. × advised me to eat pears, so I bought them and ate them too. Later, the school doctor said that I had caught a cold and it would be good to take some medicine. He poured out a dozen gray, round and flat pills from the medicine bottle. He said to take one every four hours. I didn't see clearly what the medicine was, so I took it and left.

However, the illness did not ease. My forehead was burning like fire, and my head was still dizzy. Some people said that pears were too cold in nature, and some people said that the pills could not be eaten. I became even more flustered. I still have many things to do urgently, and several friends have entrusted me to do things!

When I am usually too busy with work, I often think: "It would be a pleasure in life to have a minor illness and steal half a day of leisure." Now that I am really sick, I know that "being free from illness is light."

I also often think that people have lived enough, and it would be so pleasant to have a great liberation once. Now I know that even a minor illness of one or two days will make it impossible to deal with public and private affairs. What about the so-called great liberation? Coming to this world, life is truly only suffering!

I wanted to go out to find a doctor for treatment, but it happened to be Sunday, and most doctors stopped seeing patients. If I wanted to make a special appointment, my illness didn't seem that serious, so I had to spend this day in endurance.

On Sundays, the dormitory is almost deserted, and I feel like I am in a dead city. It was hard to wait from dawn to dusk. The lonely Sunday finally passed in unbearable endurance.

That night, I sweated again, and my whole body seemed much lighter.

The next day (Monday), I asked the school for a day off and went to see a doctor at about ten o'clock. I have always been reluctant to ask people for leave. Even if I am sick, I will never ask for leave if I can barely support myself; it was the same when I was a student. I remember that I had also received a commendation for "diligence in study and never giving up" for four semesters in senior elementary school. One semester, because I occasionally suffered from a minor illness, the teachers repeatedly urged me to ask for leave, but I finally gave up the honor of being diligent in study and never gave up and still kept that commendation.

I entered the doctor's office. The doctor slightly took my pulse, looked at my tongue coating, and asked me a few questions. He picked up a pen and wrote: "External invasion of wind evil accompanied by dampness stagnation, body heat, body cold, headache, bone pain, thin greasy tongue, slippery and rapid pulse, it is appropriate to dispel evil and transform dampness." He also prescribed several medicines, and the matter was over.

At a little after one o'clock, the pharmacy had already sent the decocted medicine. The first and second decoctions were packed separately in small thermos bottles. The taste of the medicine was so bitter, but I had to open my throat wide and pour it straight down. Once, I almost vomited it out, but I finally stopped it with the greatest suppression and did not actually vomit.

It only takes three or four days to cure a minor illness. On the fifth day, I thought my illness was cured, so I dressed and got up in a grand manner, and went to the latrine and dining hall as usual. However, when I urinated in the latrine, the color of the urine was as red as eggplant skin wine, which was a bit scary. When I went to the dining hall to eat, I only had half a bowl of rice. People said that I had lost a lot of weight after four days of illness. I also felt a bit that way myself. When I stood on the scale, I weighed only 104 pounds, whereas I was originally a thin body of 108 pounds. Although it was not as pitiful as "people are thinner than yellow flowers," it did make me feel that my body was too unusable. Fortunately, my heart has gradually aged over the years, and that ambition no longer needs this flimsy body.

Special Article

Overseas Chinese Around the World (End) 213

— Zhong Minyi

However, among these three reasons, the most important is the last one. Because if our national power is strong, even if people in various places are jealous of overseas Chinese and want to exclude them, they will not dare to deal with them casually. We see that there are many expatriates from countries such as Britain, the United States, France, and Italy in various parts of the world, right? Isn't their power great in some places? But they have never been excluded or oppressed by others. Needless to say, the reason is that their countries are rich and strong, and others do not dare to deal with them casually.

Therefore, if our overseas Chinese affairs are to develop in the future, and if our more than 10 million overseas Chinese compatriots are to have a bright future, we can only strive to rescue our country from the state of semi-colonialism and keep pace with the advanced countries in the world. Only when our international status is improved can the status of our overseas Chinese in various parts of the world be raised, and they will not be unreasonably oppressed and excluded. If we cannot get rid of the title of weak nation, then overseas Chinese will be inferior to Jews in the world and will be oppressed everywhere.

Now, not to mention Britain and the United States, even black people in Africa and the Americas, and even equally weak nations such as Siam and Annam, will also arbitrarily bully our overseas Chinese compatriots. Chinese people and even Chinese goods in the world seem to be very problematic. Even eggs recently shipped to Britain have been described as bad eggs! In such a situation, if we do not strive to rescue the country and rescue the nation, not only will overseas Chinese not be able to gain a foothold in the world in the future, but even our country and nation will soon be unable to survive!

News 216

"Shanghai Radio" is published by the Shanghai Radio Research Society, Wangfu Lane, Nanjing Road (3rd floor of Siming Savings Association), this city. The inaugural issue will be released on November 5th, selling for only one dime per issue. The content includes various wireless radio theories, knowledge, experimental circuits, experimental results reports, various machine installation methods, and repair work conditions. The writing is simple and strives to avoid superficiality, allowing readers to obtain practical knowledge at a small cost. There is also a "Broadcast Circle" column, publishing radio station broadcast news, singer photos and their works, etc. The annual subscription for twelve issues is only one yuan, and the deadline is approaching. Subscribers should not miss the opportunity.

Movie News

Introduction to "The Jazz Singer" 217

This is a new attempt by MGM. "The Jazz Singer" is originally a musical comedy that is purely a combination of aesthetic musical effects, romantic color schemes, and hilarious jokes. The leading actor is the famous "jazz" music inventor Ted Lewis, and his entire band also participates in the performance. The female lead is Vicki Bairros, and the singer, Halle Stowell, is a very popular singing star on radio broadcasts (this film is Halle's creation). In addition, there are the new comedy duo Tate Shirley and Nard Panton, and the old comedy duo Laurel and Hardy also contribute their latest masterpiece "Retribution." Opening today in Nanjing.
